The Proof for Trustworthiness in Prophets
Sanusi presents a proof for prophetic trustworthiness and clarifies its legal basis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that prophets must be trustworthy and why it is considered a legal rather than purely rational argument.

Core Idea
If prophets could betray, following them would require us to sin—but Allah never commands sin.

This lesson examines a key proof from Sanusi establishing that prophets are inherently trustworthy. The proof uses a conditional argument based on the divine command to follow prophets. It also addresses the nature of the proof, clarifying that it is not purely rational but rooted in revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the conditional structure: if prophets betray, then we would be commanded to follow them in that act.
Pay attention to the three categories of acts mentioned.
2
Identify the three act categories
Note the three types of acts that are excluded from prophets: forbidden (حرام), disliked (مكروه), and contrary to the better choice (خلاف الأولى).
3
Understand the proof's nature
Consider why the author says this proof is a legal proof (دليل شرعي) despite its rational appearance. The key is that the premises come from revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودليل وجوبِ الأمانة لهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام : أنَّهم لو خانوا بفعل محرَّمِ أو مكروه أو خلافِ الأولى، لكنَّا مأمورين به؛ لأنَّ الله تعالى أمرنا باتباعهم في أقوالهم وأفعالهم وأحوالهم من غير تفصيل، وهو تعالى لا يأمر بمحرم ولا مكروه ولا خلاف الأولى، فلا تكون أفعالهم محرمة ولا مكروهةً ولا خلاف الأولى، وهذا الدليل وإن كان على صورة الدليل العقلي هو في الحقيقة دليل شرعي ; لأنَّ دليل الملازمة شرعي، وبطلان التالي بدليل شرعي ; وهو أن الله لا يأمر بالفحشاء.
And the proof for the obligation of trustworthiness for them (peace and blessings be upon them) is that if they were to betray by committing a forbidden act, or a disliked act, or an act contrary to the better choice, then we would be commanded to do it; because Allah the Exalted has commanded us to follow them in their sayings, actions, and states without specification, and He, the Exalted, does not command a forbidden act, nor a disliked act, nor an act contrary to the better choice. So their actions are not forbidden, nor disliked, nor contrary to the better choice. And this proof, even if it appears in the form of a rational proof, is in reality a legal proof, because the premise of the implication is legal, and the falsity of the consequent is by a legal proof, which is that Allah does not command indecency.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the obligation of trustworthiness (الأمانة) for prophets. The proof is structured as a conditional: If prophets were to betray (commit a forbidden, disliked, or less preferred act), then we would be commanded to do that act, because Allah has commanded us to follow them in all sayings, actions, and states without exception. But Allah does not command any forbidden, disliked, or less preferred act. Therefore, their actions are free from such. The author notes that although the proof appears rational, it is actually a legal proof because the premise of the implication (that we are commanded to follow them) is from revelation, and the negation of the consequent (that Allah does not command evil) is also from revelation.

Key Terms
الأمانة
محرم
مكروه
خلاف الأولى
دليل عقلي
دليل شرعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This proof is a purely rational proof (دليل عقلي) because it uses logical conditional reasoning.
Correction: The author clarifies that although it appears rational, it is actually a legal proof (دليل شرعي) because its premises (the command to follow prophets and that Allah does not command evil) come from revelation, not pure reason.

Checkpoint
According to the proof, why can prophets not commit forbidden acts?
A) Because they are naturally perfect.
B) Because Allah commands us to follow them and He does not command evil.
C) Because they would lose their status.
D) Because they have no free will.

Key Takeaway
The prophet's trustworthiness is proven by the fact that following them would otherwise entail obeying commands to sin, which is impossible from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a command from the Prophet ﷺ that goes against your desires, do you truly believe he could never betray you, or do you quietly assume the command might be negotiable? How does this proof expose the inconsistency in your obedience?
?
Reflect on a specific instance where you chose an easier, less preferred action over a stronger Sunnah (e.g., praying in a less preferred way or skipping a recommended fast). In light of this lesson, does that choice reflect a subtle doubt about the Prophet's trustworthiness? What will you change starting today?
?
If you were to stand before Allah tomorrow and He asked you, 'Did you follow My Prophet without exception?', what would He find in your heart? Does this lesson not demand that you stop excusing your selective obedience and commit to unconditional emulation?

Defining Prophetic Truthfulness and Addressing an Objection
Defines truthfulness and answers an objection via the concept of insha'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars define prophetic truthfulness and how they answer the objection from the palm tree incident.

Core Idea
Truthfulness is correspondence with reality; expressions of hope are not reports.

The author begins by defining prophetic truthfulness as the correspondence of their reports with reality, even if only according to their belief. He then addresses a potential objection: the Prophet's statement to palm tree growers, which seems to be a false prediction. The answer clarifies that this statement was a construction (insha'), an expression of hope, not a factual report, and thus not subject to truth or falsehood.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of truthfulness
Read the Arabic definition carefully: truthfulness is the correspondence of the report with reality, even if according to their belief. Note that the Prophet's words 'All that did not happen' are an example of truthfulness according to his belief.
2
Study the objection and answer
Read the objection about the palm tree incident. The answer explains that the Prophet's statement was a construction (insha'), not a report, so it is not evaluated as true or false.
Understand the distinction between reports (khabar) and constructions (insha').
3
Reflect on why the objection fails
Consider why the non-occurrence of the hoped outcome does not harm the Prophet's truthfulness. The key is that the statement was not a claim about reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَصِدْقُهُمْ) معطوف على الأمانة; أي: وواجبٌ في حقهم صدقهم; وهو مطابقة خبرهم للواقع، ولو بحسب اعتقادهم، كما في قوله : «كل ذلك لم يكن» لما قال له ذو اليدين : أقصرتِ الصلاةُ أم نسيت يا رسول الله? حين سلَّم من ركعتين (١).
فإن قيل : «قد مرَّ على جماعةٍ يُؤَبِّرون النخل، وقال لهم : لو تركتموها لصلحت، فتركوها فشاصت» (٢)، أجيب أن هذا من قبيل الإنشاء; لأنَّ المعنى : كان في رجائي ذلك، والإنشاء لا يتصف بصدق ولا كذب، وعدم وقوع المُترجى لا يعد نقصاً، ودليل وجوب صدقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام أنهم لو لم يصدقوا للزم الكذب في خبره تعالى لتصديقه تعالى لهم بالمعجزة النازلة منزلة قوله تعالى : (صدق عبدي في كل ما يبلغ عني)، وتصديق الكاذب كذب; وهو محال في حقه تعالى، فملزومه وهو عدم صدقهم محال ، وإذا استحال عدم صدقهم وجب صدقهم وهو المطلوب، لكن هذا الدليل إنما يدلُّ على صدقهم في دعوى الرسالة وفي الأحكام الشرعية; لأن ذلك هو الذي بلغوه عن الله تعالى ولا يدل على صدقهم في غير ذلك كـ (قام زيد، وقعد عمرو)، ولكن يدل عليه دليل الأمانة; لأنه داخل فيها، ولو التفت لعموم الأمانة ما بعدها، وعُلم من ذلك أنَّ أقسام الصدق ثلاثة، والمقصود هنا جميع الأولان، وأما الثالث فهو داخل في الأمانة كما علمت.
His saying: 'and their truthfulness' is conjoined to trustworthiness; i.e., obligatory in their right is their truthfulness, which is the correspondence of their report with reality, even if according to their belief, as in his saying: 'All that did not happen' when Dhu al-Yadayn said to him: 'Was the prayer shortened or did you forget, O Messenger of Allah?' when he had given the salam after two rak'ahs (1). If it is said: 'He passed by a group pollinating palm trees and said to them: If you leave them, they will be fine, so they left them and they became spoiled' (2), the answer is that this is of the category of construction (insha'), because the meaning is: that was my hope; and construction is not described as true or false, and the non-occurrence of what is hoped for does not constitute a deficiency. And the proof for the obligation of their truthfulness (peace and blessings be upon them) is that if they were not truthful, then falsehood would be necessary in the news of Allah the Exalted, due to His confirmation of them through the miracle, which is in the position of His saying: 'My servant is truthful in all he conveys from Me.' And confirming a liar is a lie; that is impossible with respect to Allah the Exalted. So its entailment—which is their lack of truthfulness—is impossible. And if their lack of truthfulness is impossible, then their truthfulness is necessary, and that is what is sought. However, this proof only indicates their truthfulness in the claim of prophethood and in legal rulings, because that is what they conveyed from Allah the Exalted, and it does not indicate their truthfulness in other matters like 'Zaid stood' or 'Amr sat.' But that is indicated by the proof of trustworthiness, because it is included in it. And if you consider the generality of trustworthiness, it covers that. And it is known from this that the categories of truthfulness are three, and what is intended here are the first two, while the third is included in trustworthiness as you have learned.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage defines truthfulness for prophets, addresses an objection, and proves its necessity. It begins by explaining that truthfulness (الصدق) is the correspondence of their report with reality, even if only according to their belief. An example is given from a hadith where the Prophet said 'All that did not happen' after a forgetful salam. Then an objection is raised: the Prophet once told palm tree growers to leave them, then they became spoiled, which might seem like a false prediction. The answer is that this statement was a construction (إنشاء), i.e., an expression of hope, not a report, so it is not evaluated as true or false. The proof for truthfulness is that if prophets were not truthful, then Allah's confirmation of them through miracles would be confirming a liar, which is impossible, so truthfulness is necessary. However, this proof only covers their truthfulness in matters of prophethood and religious rulings; other matters are covered by the proof of trustworthiness. The passage ends by noting that there are three categories of truthfulness, and the intent here includes the first two, while the third falls under trustworthiness.

Key Terms
الصدق
الإنشاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the Prophet made a false prediction about the palm trees, thus violating truthfulness.
Correction: The statement was an expression of hope, not a report of future fact, so it does not involve truth or falsehood.

Checkpoint
How does the author answer the objection about the Prophet's statement to the palm tree growers?
A) The Prophet made a mistake.
B) The statement was a construction (إنشاء), not a report.
C) The growers misunderstood.
D) The hadith is weak.

Key Takeaway
Prophetic truthfulness is defined as correspondence with reality, and statements of hope are not reports, so they neither confirm nor violate truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you speak about something you are not certain of, do you present it as a fact or as a hope? How does the distinction between khabar and insha' challenge the way you communicate with others about future events?
?
The Prophet’s truthfulness was upheld even in a statement based on his belief. Reflect on a time you stated something as true that you later discovered was false. Did you intend it as a report or as an expression of hope? What will you change in how you speak about uncertain matters?
?
If your words were judged by the standard of correspondence with reality, how many of your daily statements would pass as truthful reports? What would it cost you to only say what you know to be true, and to frame everything else as hope or opinion?

The Proof for Prophetic Truthfulness and Its Scope
Presents the proof for truthfulness and clarifies its scope and categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proof from divine confirmation for prophetic truthfulness and its limitation to religious matters.

Core Idea
Allah's confirmation via miracles proves prophets truthful in revelation; trustworthiness covers other statements.

After establishing the definition and addressing an objection, the author now provides the rational proof that prophetic truthfulness is obligatory. The proof hinges on the fact that Allah confirms prophets by miracles, which would be impossible if they were liars. However, this proof only applies to their messages about prophethood and religious rulings; other statements are covered by the proof of trustworthiness.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof for truthfulness
Read the logical argument: if prophets were not truthful, then Allah's confirmation through miracles would be confirming a liar, which is impossible, so truthfulness is necessary.
Notice the phrase 'نازلة منزلة قوله تعالى: صدق عبدي'.
2
Understand the scope of the proof
The proof only guarantees truthfulness in matters of prophethood and religious rulings (what they convey from Allah). It does not cover statements about everyday matters.
The author says: 'لكن هذا الدليل إنما يدل على صدقهم في دعوى الرسالة وفي الأحكام الشرعية'.
3
Learn about the three categories of truthfulness
The passage concludes by stating that there are three categories of truthfulness. The first two are covered by this proof, and the third is covered by trustworthiness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَصِدْقُهُمْ) معطوف على الأمانة; أي: وواجبٌ في حقهم صدقهم; وهو مطابقة خبرهم للواقع، ولو بحسب اعتقادهم، كما في قوله : «كل ذلك لم يكن» لما قال له ذو اليدين : أقصرتِ الصلاةُ أم نسيت يا رسول الله? حين سلَّم من ركعتين (١).
فإن قيل : «قد مرَّ على جماعةٍ يُؤَبِّرون النخل، وقال لهم : لو تركتموها لصلحت، فتركوها فشاصت» (٢)، أجيب أن هذا من قبيل الإنشاء; لأنَّ المعنى : كان في رجائي ذلك، والإنشاء لا يتصف بصدق ولا كذب، وعدم وقوع المُترجى لا يعد نقصاً، ودليل وجوب صدقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام أنهم لو لم يصدقوا للزم الكذب في خبره تعالى لتصديقه تعالى لهم بالمعجزة النازلة منزلة قوله تعالى : (صدق عبدي في كل ما يبلغ عني)، وتصديق الكاذب كذب; وهو محال في حقه تعالى، فملزومه وهو عدم صدقهم محال ، وإذا استحال عدم صدقهم وجب صدقهم وهو المطلوب، لكن هذا الدليل إنما يدلُّ على صدقهم في دعوى الرسالة وفي الأحكام الشرعية; لأن ذلك هو الذي بلغوه عن الله تعالى ولا يدل على صدقهم في غير ذلك كـ (قام زيد، وقعد عمرو)، ولكن يدل عليه دليل الأمانة; لأنه داخل فيها، ولو التفت لعموم الأمانة ما بعدها، وعُلم من ذلك أنَّ أقسام الصدق ثلاثة، والمقصود هنا جميع الأولان، وأما الثالث فهو داخل في الأمانة كما علمت.
His saying: 'and their truthfulness' is conjoined to trustworthiness; i.e., obligatory in their right is their truthfulness, which is the correspondence of their report with reality, even if according to their belief, as in his saying: 'All that did not happen' when Dhu al-Yadayn said to him: 'Was the prayer shortened or did you forget, O Messenger of Allah?' when he had given the salam after two rak'ahs (1). If it is said: 'He passed by a group pollinating palm trees and said to them: If you leave them, they will be fine, so they left them and they became spoiled' (2), the answer is that this is of the category of construction (insha'), because the meaning is: that was my hope; and construction is not described as true or false, and the non-occurrence of what is hoped for does not constitute a deficiency. And the proof for the obligation of their truthfulness (peace and blessings be upon them) is that if they were not truthful, then falsehood would be necessary in the news of Allah the Exalted, due to His confirmation of them through the miracle, which is in the position of His saying: 'My servant is truthful in all he conveys from Me.' And confirming a liar is a lie; that is impossible with respect to Allah the Exalted. So its entailment—which is their lack of truthfulness—is impossible. And if their lack of truthfulness is impossible, then their truthfulness is necessary, and that is what is sought. However, this proof only indicates their truthfulness in the claim of prophethood and in legal rulings, because that is what they conveyed from Allah the Exalted, and it does not indicate their truthfulness in other matters like 'Zaid stood' or 'Amr sat.' But that is indicated by the proof of trustworthiness, because it is included in it. And if you consider the generality of trustworthiness, it covers that. And it is known from this that the categories of truthfulness are three, and what is intended here are the first two, while the third is included in trustworthiness as you have learned.

Commentary
This passage defines truthfulness for prophets, addresses an objection, and proves its necessity. It begins by explaining that truthfulness (الصدق) is the correspondence of their report with reality, even if only according to their belief. An example is given from a hadith where the Prophet said 'All that did not happen' after a forgetful salam. Then an objection is raised: the Prophet once told palm tree growers to leave them, then they became spoiled, which might seem like a false prediction. The answer is that this statement was a construction (إنشاء), i.e., an expression of hope, not a report, so it is not evaluated as true or false. The proof for truthfulness is that if prophets were not truthful, then Allah's confirmation of them through miracles would be confirming a liar, which is impossible, so truthfulness is necessary. However, this proof only covers their truthfulness in matters of prophethood and religious rulings; other matters are covered by the proof of trustworthiness. The passage ends by noting that there are three categories of truthfulness, and the intent here includes the first two, while the third falls under trustworthiness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that prophets must be truthful in every statement, including mundane remarks like 'Zaid stood'.
Correction: The miracle-based proof only guarantees truthfulness in their religious teachings; everyday statements are covered by trustworthiness, which is a broader attribute.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say the proof for truthfulness does not apply to statements like 'Zaid stood'?
A) Such statements are not reported from prophets.
B) The proof only covers what they convey from Allah.
C) Those statements are not subject to truth or falsehood.
D) The proof is weak.

Key Takeaway
The miracle-based proof establishes prophetic truthfulness in religious matters, while everyday truthfulness falls under trustworthiness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof shows that Allah would never confirm a liar, so He confirmed the prophets with miracles. Have you fully accepted the teachings of the prophets, or do you sometimes doubt or reject parts of what they conveyed because they don't align with your desires? What would it mean for your faith if you are actually rejecting the truth that Allah Himself confirmed? Commit today to studying one prophetic teaching you have avoided.
?
If Allah considered confirming a liar as repugnant, how do you feel about your own role in confirming falsehood? When you remain silent about a lie, spread gossip, or approve of dishonesty for convenience, you are effectively confirming a liar. How will you change your speech and actions today to be a person who upholds truth even when it is difficult?

The Correct Interpretation of the Prophet's Marriage to Zaynab
Sanusi transmits the authoritative interpretation of the Prophetic marriage to Zaynab and refutes a false allegation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the authoritative Sunni interpretation of the verse regarding the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab and why alternative interpretations are rejected.

Core Idea
The Prophet's marriage to Zaynab was by divine command, not personal desire.

The verse concerning the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab bint Jahsh has been subject to misinterpretation. In this passage, the commentator provides the soundest interpretation, tracing it back to 'Ali ibn al-Husayn, and clarifies the meaning of key terms like 'khashyah'. This lesson will help you grasp the correct theological stance on this event.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Note the flow from stating the soundest interpretation to refuting a false claim.
2
Identify the key interpretation
The passage states that the soundest interpretation is that Allah informed the Prophet that Zaynab would be his wife. Find this part and understand the sequence of events.
3
Understand the meaning of 'khashyah'
The passage explains that 'khashyah' in this context means shyness from people, not fear of sin or desire. See how this fits the narrative.
4
Refute the misconception
The passage explicitly refutes the claim that the Prophet concealed a sinful desire. It argues that even the least of awliya' would not do such a thing. Understand this argument.
This is a key doctrinal point.
5
Affirm the correct belief
The passage concludes by stating that this is what we believe and worship Allah with, as transmitted by al-Sanusi. Reflect on the importance of holding this belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأصح محامله ما نقله من يُعوّل عليه في التفسير عن علي بن الحسين : من أن الله تعالى كان أعلم نبيَّه أن زينب ستكون من أزواجه، فلما شكاها إليه زيد، فقال له : أمسك عليك زوجك، واتق الله، وأخفى في نفسه ما أعلمه الله به من أنه سيتزوجها والله مُبدي ذلك بطلاق زيد لها، وتزويجها له، ومعنى الخشية استحياؤُه من الناس أن يقولوا : تزوّج زوجة ابنه ؛ أي: مَنْ تبناه، فعاتبه الله على هذا الاستحياء لعلو مقامه وما قيل: من أنه تعلَّق قلبه بها، وأخفاه فلا يلتفت إليه، وإن جلَّ ناقلوه (۱) ، فإن أدنى الأولياء لا يصدر عنه مثل هذا الأمر، فما بالك به ، وهذا هو الذي نعتقده وندين الله به كما نقله السنوسي في كتبه .
And the soundest of its interpretations is what is transmitted by one who is relied upon in tafsir from 'Ali ibn al-Husayn: that Allah Almighty had informed His Prophet that Zaynab would be among his wives, so when Zayd complained about her to him, he said to him: 'Keep your wife and fear Allah,' and he concealed within himself what Allah had informed him of, that he would marry her, and Allah would bring that about through Zayd divorcing her and her marriage to him. And the meaning of 'fear' [khashyah] was his shyness from the people, lest they say: 'He married the wife of his son' — i.e., of the one he had adopted. So Allah reproached him for this shyness due to the loftiness of his station. And as for what was said — that his heart inclined to her and he concealed it — no attention is paid to it, even if its transmitters are great, for the least of the awliya' would not do such a thing, so what about him? This is what we believe and by which we worship Allah, as transmitted by al-Sanusi in his books.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage provides the authoritative Sunni interpretation of the verse concerning the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab bint Jahsh. It begins by stating that the soundest interpretation is the one transmitted from 'Ali ibn al-Husayn (Zayn al-'Abidin). The explanation is that Allah informed the Prophet that Zaynab would be among his wives. When Zayd, the Prophet's adopted son, complained about Zaynab, the Prophet told him to keep his wife and fear Allah, while concealing the knowledge that she would eventually become his wife. The term 'khashyah' in the verse is interpreted as shyness from people, who might say that he married the wife of his adopted son. Allah reproached the Prophet for this shyness because of his lofty station. The passage then refutes the claim that the Prophet had a secret desire for Zaynab, stating that even the least of Allah's saints would not commit such an act, so how could the Prophet? It concludes by affirming that this is the correct belief and the one held by al-Sanusi in his works.

Key Terms
محامل
خشية
استحياء
التبني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet had a secret romantic desire for Zaynab and concealed it.
Correction: The correct interpretation is that the Prophet concealed the divine knowledge that she would become his wife, not any personal desire. Even the lowest saint would not act on such desire, so how could the Prophet?

Checkpoint
What is the meaning of 'khashyah' in the verse according to the correct interpretation?
A) Fear of Allah
B) Shyness from people
C) Fear of sin
D) Concealment of love

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's marriage to Zaynab was by divine decree, and his 'fear' was modesty before people, not secret desire.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation that requires you to obey Allah but risks human disapproval, what is your first instinct? Does the Prophet's experience—being reproached for a permissible shyness—make you reevaluate your own priorities?
?
The Prophet concealed nothing but divine knowledge. Think of a time you concealed something. Was your motive fear of people or fear of Allah? Can you, right now, resolve to speak the truth even if it costs you your reputation?
?
If even the least saint would not act on hidden desire, what does that say about your own heart's inclinations? Are you willing to hold yourself to the standard of the awliya' by purifying your intentions before Allah?

Impossible Attributes for Messengers
Definition of four impossible attributes and their basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four attributes that are impossible for messengers and why their impossibility is based on transmitted evidence rather than pure reason.

Core Idea
Messengers are protected by transmitted evidence from their opposites.

This passage completes the picture of prophetic attributes by identifying what cannot be found in a messenger. Just as there are four essential attributes that a messenger must possess, there are four corresponding opposites that must be absent. The author also clarifies the nature of this impossibility—it is not a logical impossibility but a revealed one, grounded in the Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the literal translation. Notice how the author defines each impossible attribute as the opposite of a necessary one.
Pay attention to the phrase 'but by transmitted evidence'—it's the key to understanding the nature of impossibility here.
2
Identify the four impossible attributes
List the four opposites mentioned: betrayal (against trustworthiness), lying (against truthfulness), heedlessness (against intelligence), and concealment (against conveying).
These are not random; they directly negate each necessary attribute.
3
Understand the basis of impossibility
The passage states that these attributes 'do not admit of affirmation' but only through transmitted evidence. Ask yourself: why is it important that this impossibility is based on revelation and not reason?
This guards against the misconception that reason alone can determine what is impossible for a messenger.
4
Connect to the phrase 'as they narrated'
The author refers to scholars narrating from the Book, Sunnah, and consensus. See how this phrase anchors the entire discussion in Islamic textual authority.
This reinforces the Sunni approach: theology is grounded in revealed sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما يستحيلُ فى حقِّ الرَّسل عليهمُ الصَّلاة والسَّلامُ] قوله : (وَيَسْتَحِيلُ ضِدُّهَا ) أي : ويستحيل في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام ضد الصفات الأربعة الواجبة في حقهم؛ فضدُّ الأمانة الخيانة، وضد الصدق الكذب، وضدُّ الفطانة الغفلة وعدم الفطنة، وضد التبليغ كتمان شيء ممَّا أُمروا بتبليغه، ومعنى استحالتها عدم قبولها الثبوت، لكن بالدليل الشرعي، كما أشار إليه بقوله : (كَمَا رووا)، فإن المعنى : لما رواه العلماء من كتاب وسنة وإجماع.
What is impossible in the case of messengers, upon them be prayer and peace — His saying: 'And their opposites are impossible' means: It is impossible in their case — upon them be prayer and peace — the opposite of the four attributes that are necessary in their case. So the opposite of trustworthiness is betrayal, the opposite of truthfulness is lying, the opposite of intelligence is heedlessness and lack of intelligence, and the opposite of conveying is concealing something of what they were commanded to convey. The meaning of their impossibility is that they do not admit of affirmation, but by transmitted evidence, as he indicated by his saying: 'as they narrated' — for the meaning is: because the scholars narrated from the Book, Sunnah, and consensus.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage defines the four attributes that are impossible for messengers, which are the opposites of the four necessary attributes. The necessary attributes for messengers are trustworthiness (amana), truthfulness (sidq), intelligence (fatana), and conveying (tabligh). Their opposites are betrayal, lying, heedlessness, and concealment. The impossibility of these attributes is not rational but based on transmitted evidence from the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, as indicated by the phrase 'as they narrated'.

Key Terms
يستحيل
ضد
أمانة
صدق
فطانة
تبليغ
الدليل الشرعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the impossibility is rational (a priori), meaning a messenger logically cannot have these opposites.
Correction: The author clarifies that the impossibility is based on transmitted evidence (Qur'an, Sunnah, consensus), not pure logic.

Checkpoint
How many attributes are impossible for messengers according to this passage?
A) 2
B) 3
C) 4
D) 5

Key Takeaway
The four impossible attributes for messengers—betrayal, lying, heedlessness, and concealment—are established as impossible through transmitted evidence from revelation and consensus, not reason alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If it is impossible for a messenger to betray or conceal any part of the message, then every command and warning they conveyed is absolutely trustworthy. How does this certainty confront your hesitation to obey a difficult command of Allah today? What one area of your life are you holding back from submitting fully, and what does that reveal about your trust in the messenger?
?
The passage ties the impossibility of these opposites specifically to transmitted evidence, not just your reasoning. Has your reliance on your own understanding ever led you to doubt something clearly conveyed by the Prophet? Will you commit to checking your doubts against the Book and Sunnah before acting on them?
?
If heedlessness (lack of intelligence) is impossible for messengers, then every word of the Prophet is precise and deliberate. How does this challenge your excuse that 'I didn’t know' or 'I forgot' about a sunnah you have neglected? What will you do this week to ensure you are not heedless of his guidance?

Concept and Examples of Permissible Attributes
Introduction to permissible attributes with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that permissible attributes of messengers are those whose existence and non-existence are both possible, and that these include both indispensable acts like eating and optional acts like intercourse.

Core Idea
Permissible attributes for messengers are normal human acts, both necessary and optional.

After covering the necessary and impossible attributes of messengers, the author now turns to the permissible ones. These are acts that are neither required nor impossible for them, but simply possible. The author gives examples to illustrate that permissible acts range from everyday necessities like eating to more optional ones like intercourse, emphasizing that these acts are not beneath the prophetic status.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get a feel for the author's style. Note that it starts with a transition from previous topics.
2
Understand the concept of 'jā'iz'
The author defines permissible as 'that whose existence and non-existence are both possible'. Notice how this contrasts with necessary and impossible.
This is a fundamental concept in kalam.
3
Analyze the examples
The author gives eating and intercourse as examples. Notice the grammatical analysis of 'ka al-akl' and the reason for repeating the example with intercourse.
The repetition is to show that permissible acts include both indispensable and dispensable ones.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وَجَائِزٌ ... إلخ) لمَّا قدَّمَ الكلام على الواجب في حقِّ الرُّسل، والمستحيل كذلك .. شرع في الكلام على الجائز في حقهم؛ لأنه كالمركب الواجب والمستحيل، فإنه ما يجوز وجوده لهم وعدمه. وقوله : (فِي حَقِّهِمْ) أي: على ذاتهم، فـ(في) بمعنى (على)، و(حق) بمعنى الذات، والضمير للرُّسل، وكذا الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام. وقوله : (كَالأَكْلِ ) أي : مثل الأكل، فالكاف اسم بمعنى (مثل)، مبتدأ مؤخّر (۱) قد تقدَّم خبره، وهو (جائز)، ويصح أن يكون فاعلاً به سد مسد الخبر، على رأي من لا يشترط الاعتماد على استفهام أو نحوه، كما في قوله : (خبير بنو لهب). وقوله : (وَكالجِمَاعِ لِلنِّسَا) بالقصر للوزن، وإنما كرّر المثال إشارة إلى أنه لا فرقَ أن يكون الجائز في حقهم من توابع الصحة التي لا يُستغنى عنها عادةً كالأكل والشرب والنوم، أو التي يُستغنى عنها كالجماع للنساء، فإنه يُستغنى عنه بدون حبس النفس حبساً شديداً، بناءً على أنه من باب التفكُهِ، أو بحبس النفس حبساً شديداً، بناءً على أنه من باب القوت. وقوله : (فِي الحِل) أي : في حال الحل بمعنى الجواز؛ بأن كان بالملك أو بالنكاح، فيجوز لهم الوطء بالملك، ولو للأمة الكتابية، بخلاف المجوسية ونحوها كالوثنية، وخالف ابن العربي في الأمة الكتابية مُعلّلاً بأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام شريف عن أن يَضعَ نطفته في رَحِم كافرة، وبأنها تكره صحبته، وأما الأمة المسلمة بالملك فجائزة باتفاقي، ويجوز لهم الوطء بالنكاح لما عدا الكتابية والمجوسية ونحوهما، وما عدا الأمة، ولو مسلمة؛ لأنها إنما تُنكح لخوف العنت ولعدم الطول أو المهر ، وكلٌّ منهما مُنتَفٍ ؛ أما الأول فللعصمة، وأما الثاني فلأنهم واجدون للطَّول ؛ أي: المهر، على أنه يجوز للنبي أن يتزوج بدون مهر، ويُعلم من كلامه في الحل) أنهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام لا يطؤوهن صائمات صوماً مشروعاً ، ولا معتكفات كذلك، ولا حائضات، ولا نفساء، ولا مُحرمات.
His saying: 'And permissible... etc.' — when he had previously discussed the necessary in the case of messengers, and the impossible likewise, he began discussing the permissible in their case, because it is like the compound of the necessary and impossible: it is that whose existence and non-existence are both possible for them. And his saying: 'in their case' means 'upon their essence', so 'fi' is in the sense of 'upon', and 'haqq' in the sense of 'essence', and the pronoun refers to the messengers, and likewise the prophets, upon them be prayer and peace. And his saying: 'like eating' means 'like eating', so the kaf is a noun meaning 'like', a delayed subject whose predicate preceded, which is 'permissible', and it is also possible that it is an actor that takes the place of the predicate, according to those who do not require dependence on an interrogative or the like, as in the saying: 'Expert are the sons of Lahab'. And his saying: 'and like intercourse with women' — with shortening for meter, and he repeated the example to indicate that there is no difference between the permissible in their case that is a corollary of health that is usually indispensable, like eating, drinking, and sleep, or that which can be dispensed with, like intercourse with women, for it can be dispensed with without severely restraining oneself, based on its being for pleasure, or with severe restraint, based on its being for sustenance. And his saying: 'in the permissible' means in a state of permissibility, i.e., by ownership or marriage. So they may have intercourse by ownership, even with a slave woman who is a Kitabi (People of the Book), unlike a Magian or the like, and Ibn al-'Arabi disagreed regarding the Kitabi slave woman, reasoning that the Prophet, peace be upon him, is too noble to place his sperm in the womb of an unbeliever, and that she would dislike his company. As for a Muslim slave woman by ownership, it is permissible by agreement. And they may have intercourse by marriage with anyone except the Kitabi and Magian and the like, and except a slave woman even if Muslim, because she is only married out of fear of sin and due to lack of means or dowry, and both are absent: the first due to infallibility, and the second because they possess means (i.e., dowry). And it is permissible for the Prophet to marry without dowry. And it is understood from his speech 'in the permissible' that they, peace be upon them, do not have intercourse with women who are fasting a legitimate fast, nor those in i'tikaf, nor menstruating, nor in postpartum bleeding, nor in ihram.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the permissible attributes of messengers. The author states that after discussing the necessary and impossible attributes, he turns to the permissible ones, which are those whose existence and non-existence are both possible for them. He clarifies linguistic points: 'fi haqqihim' means 'upon their essence', and the example 'ka al-akl' (like eating) is analyzed grammatically. He then explains why the example of intercourse is given: to show that the permissible can include things that are normally indispensable (like eating) and things that can be dispensed with (like intercourse). He then discusses the conditions for intercourse: it must be in a permissible context, either by ownership (concubinage) or marriage. For ownership, even a Kitabi slave woman is allowed, though Ibn al-'Arabi disagreed. For marriage, they cannot marry Kitabi or Magian women, nor slave women (even Muslim) because the reasons for marrying a slave are absent in the prophets. He also notes that prophets can marry without dowry. Finally, he deduces that prophets do not have intercourse with women who are fasting, in i'tikaf, menstruating, postpartum, or in ihram.

Key Terms
جائز
الأكل
الجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Permissible attributes are limited to necessary acts like eating.
Correction: The author shows that permissible acts include both necessary and optional acts, such as intercourse.

Checkpoint
What is the definition of permissible attributes according to the passage?
A) Acts that must exist for messengers.
B) Acts that cannot exist for messengers.
C) Acts whose existence and non-existence are both possible.
D) Acts that are unique to prophets.

Key Takeaway
Permissible attributes for messengers are those acts that are neither compulsory nor impossible for them, ranging from everyday necessities to optional human actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that prophets ate and married like you. Does your daily routine—your meals, your marriage—reflect that these are not barriers to closeness with Allah but opportunities? What is one habit you will change today to make an ordinary act an act of worship?

?
If you truly believed that a prophet could engage in the same human needs you do without diminishing his rank, would you still make excuses for your own negligence? What stops you from seeing your humanity as a means of obedience rather than an obstacle?

Rules of Intercourse for Messengers: Ownership, Marriage, and Restrictions
Detailed rules for prophets' intercourse by ownership and marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the conditions and limitations on prophets having intercourse by ownership or marriage, and the situations in which it is not permitted.

Core Idea
Prophets' marital relations are bound by specific rules preserving dignity and avoiding prohibited situations.

Having established that intercourse is a permissible act for messengers, the author now delves into its specific regulations. He explains that it must be within a lawful contract—either ownership (concubinage) or marriage—and he discusses exceptions and disagreements, such as the case of Kitabi slave women. He also outlines prohibitions during states like fasting, i'tikaf, and menstruation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on conditions
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'فِي الحِل' up to the end. It details the two lawful ways for intercourse and the exceptions.
2
Distinguish between ownership and marriage
Note that by ownership, a prophet can have intercourse even with a Kitabi slave woman, but by marriage, he cannot marry Kitabi or Magian women.
This distinction is crucial.
3
Review the disagreement with Ibn al-Arabi
Ibn al-Arabi argued against intercourse with Kitabi slave women, but the author presents his view without endorsing it.
This shows there is scholarly difference.
4
Understand the restrictions
The author deduces from 'fi al-hill' that prophets do not have intercourse when the woman is fasting, in i'tikaf, menstruating, etc.
These are standard Islamic legal restrictions.

Prophets and Wet Dreams: The Satanic Origin
Clarification on prophetic wet dreams due to satanic origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why wet dreams are considered impossible for prophets according to classical Islamic theology, and the distinction between satanic and natural emissions.

Core Idea
Wet dreams are from Satan, thus impossible for prophets.

This passage tackles a subtle point about prophetic impeccability. It clarifies that while wet dreams are attributed to Satan and therefore impossible for prophets, a purely natural fluid emission without satanic involvement is not prohibited. This distinction preserves the prophets' purity without denying their full humanity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Note that the passage first states the ruling (forbidden) and then provides the reason (from Satan) and a supporting hadith.
The passage is truncated but the main points are clear.
2
Identify the rule and exception
Identify the two parts: (1) Wet dreams are impossible for prophets because they are from Satan. (2) However, a mere flow of fluid without satanic manipulation is not prohibited.
This shows a nuanced understanding: not all emissions are equal.
3
Connect to broader theology
Reflect on why this matters: prophets are protected from satanic influences, yet they experience normal human attributes that do not imply deficiency.
This preserves both their purity and their humanity.

Permissible Acts for Prophets: Necessities and Options
Classification of permissible human acts for prophets into necessary and optional.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author classifies permissible human acts for prophets into necessary (indispensable) and optional (dispensable) categories, and why the example of intercourse is used to illustrate the optional category.

Core Idea
Prophets can engage in both necessary acts and optional pleasures; both are equally permissible.

This lesson unpacks a key passage that clarifies the scope of permissible actions for prophets. The author uses the example of intercourse to demonstrate that some acts are indispensable for health, while others are optional pleasures that can be forgone. Understanding this classification prevents misunderstanding about prophetic behavior and their engagement with worldly matters.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the author's mention of 'jā'iz' and the example of intercourse. The passage is dense, so take your time.
The passage includes a grammatical point about the word 'jā'iz' serving as a predicate substitute.
2
Identify the two categories
The passage explicitly distinguishes between two types of permissible acts: those that are 'min tawābi' al-ṣiḥḥa allatī lā yustaghnā ʿanhā ʿādatan' (necessities of health that are commonly indispensable) and those 'allatī yustaghnā ʿanhā' (that can be dispensed with). List examples given for each.
Examples: eating, drinking, sleeping are necessary; intercourse is optional.
3
Analyze the example of intercourse
The author explains that intercourse can be considered either a form of pleasure (tafakkuh) or sustenance (qūt). Note how the degree of difficulty in abstaining differs based on this categorization.
This shows that optional acts are still permissible, not forbidden.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قد تقدَّم خبره، وهو (جائز)، ويصح أن يكون فاعلاً به سد مسد الخبر، على رأي من لا يشترط الاعتماد على استفهام أو نحوه، كما في قوله : (خبير بنو لهب). وقوله : (وَكالجِمَاعِ لِلنِّسَا) بالقصر للوزن، وإنما كرّر المثال إشارة إلى أنه لا فرقَ أن يكون الجائز في حقهم من توابع الصحة التي لا يُستغنى عنها عادةً كالأكل والشرب والنوم، أو التي يُستغنى عنها كالجماع للنساء، فإنه يُستغنى عنه بدون حبس النفس حبساً شديداً، بناءً على أنه من باب التفكُهِ، أو بحبس النفس حبساً شديداً، بناءً على أنه من باب القوت.
It has already been mentioned before, and it is (permissible), and it is correct that it (the verb) acts as a substitute for the predicate, according to the view of those who do not require reliance on an interrogative or the like, as in his statement: (Khabīr banū lahb). And his statement: (And like intercourse with women) with shortening for meter. He only repeated the example to indicate that there is no difference whether the permissible in their case is from the necessities of health that are commonly indispensable, like eating, drinking, and sleeping, or that which can be dispensed with, like intercourse with women, for it can be dispensed with without severely restraining oneself, based on it being a matter of pleasure, or by severely restraining oneself, based on it being a matter of sustenance.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a classification of permissible human acts for prophets. The author begins by noting that the word 'jā'iz' (permissible) has already been mentioned, and he explains its syntactic role. He then uses the example of 'intercourse with women' to illustrate that permissible acts fall into two categories: those that are necessary for health and cannot be avoided, like eating, drinking, and sleeping; and those that are optional and can be abstained from, like sexual intercourse. The latter can be forgone either with mild difficulty (if considered a pleasure) or with severe difficulty (if considered a form of sustenance). The example is repeated to emphasize that both categories are equally permissible for prophets.

Correction: The passage clarifies that optional pleasures like intercourse are permissible for prophets and that there is no difference in permissibility between necessary acts and optional acts.

Checkpoint

B) It is permissible only if necessary for health.

Key Takeaway
The passage establishes that permissible acts for prophets include both indispensable health necessities and optional pleasures, with no difference in permissibility.

Permissible Relations for Prophets: Ownership and Marriage
Author details the rules of permissible sexual relations for prophets through ownership and marriage, with exceptions and derived rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific rules governing permissible sexual relations for prophets, including the categories of ownership and marriage, the exceptions based on faith and status, and the derived prohibitions on certain states.

Core Idea
Prophets' permissible relations have strict boundaries based on faith, status, and ritual states.

This passage from the Tuhfa explains the detailed fiqh rulings on what is permissible for prophets in terms of sexual relations. The author clarifies that permissibility is defined through either ownership or marriage, with specific conditions and exceptions. Understanding these rules deepens our appreciation of the prophets' special status and the wisdom behind these divine laws.

Guided Path
1
Understand the meaning of 'fī al-ḥill'
The passage begins by explaining that permissibility (ḥill) is through ownership or marriage. This sets the foundation for the detailed rules that follow.
The term 'fī al-ḥill' is a key phrase indicating a state of permissibility.
2
Explore the rules of ownership
Read how prophets may have intercourse with slave women, including the permissibility with a Kitābiyyah and the dissent by Ibn al-‘Arabī. Notice the exception for Majūsiyyah and idolatresses.
Ibn al-‘Arabī's reasoning highlights the prophetic nobility.
3
Examine the rules of marriage
Learn which women prophets may marry (free, non-Kitābiyyah/non-Majūsiyyah) and why they cannot marry slave women, even Muslims. The reasons are the absence of fear of fornication and lack of dowry.
4
Note the special allowance for dowry
Prophets may marry without a dowry, emphasizing their unique status and ability to provide.
5
Derive prohibitions from the principle
From the statement 'fī al-ḥill' we infer that prophets do not have intercourse with wives during states that negate permissibility, such as fasting, i‘tikāf, menstruation, etc.
This is a derived ruling based on the general condition of 'ḥill'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله : (فِي الحِل) أي : في حال الحل بمعنى الجواز؛ بأن كان بالملك أو بالنكاح، فيجوز لهم الوطء بالملك، ولو للأمة الكتابية، بخلاف المجوسية ونحوها كالوثنية، وخالف ابن العربي في الأمة الكتابية مُعلّلاً بأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام شريف عن أن يَضعَ نطفته في رَحِم كافرة، وبأنها تكره صحبته، وأما الأمة المسلمة بالملك فجائزة باتفاقي، ويجوز لهم الوطء بالنكاح لما عدا الكتابية والمجوسية ونحوهما، وما عدا الأمة، ولو مسلمة؛ لأنها إنما تُنكح لخوف العنت ولعدم الطول أو المهر ، وكلٌّ منهما مُنْتَفٍ ؛ أما الأول فللعصمة، وأما الثاني فلأنهم واجدون للطَّول ؛ أي: المهر، على أنه يجوز للنبي أن يتزوج بدون مهر، ويُعلم من كلامه في الحل) أنهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام لا يطؤونهن صائمات صوماً مشروعاً ، ولا معتكفات كذلك، ولا حائضات، ولا نفساء، ولا مُحرمات.
And his statement: (fī al-ḥill) meaning in the state of permissibility, meaning permissibility; whether through ownership or marriage, so they may have intercourse through ownership, even with a kitābiyyah slave woman, contrary to a majūsiyyah or the like like an idolatress. Ibn al-‘Arabī dissented regarding the kitābiyyah slave woman, reasoning that the Prophet (peace be upon him) is too noble to place his seed in the womb of an unbeliever, and that she would dislike his company. As for a Muslim slave woman through ownership, it is permissible by agreement. And they may have intercourse through marriage with other than the kitābiyyah and majūsiyyah and the like, and other than the slave woman, even if Muslim; because she is only married for fear of fornication and lack of means or dowry, and both are absent: as for the first due to infallibility, and as for the second because they possess the means, i.e. dowry, and the Prophet may marry without dowry. And it is understood from his statement 'in the state of permissibility' that they (peace be upon them) do not have intercourse with them while fasting a legitimate fast, nor while in i‘tikāf, nor while menstruating, nor in post-natal bleeding, nor in iḥrām.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal ruling on permissible sexual relations for prophets. It first explains that the phrase 'fī al-ḥill' means in a state of permissibility, whether through ownership (milk) or marriage (nikāḥ). Through ownership, a prophet may have intercourse with a slave woman who is a Kitābiyyah (Jewish or Christian), but not a Majūsiyyah (Zoroastrian) or idolatress. Ibn al-‘Arabī objected to the Kitābiyyah case, arguing that the Prophet is too noble for his seed to be placed in a disbeliever's womb and that she would dislike his company. However, the consensus (according to the author) is that it is permissible. Through marriage, prophets may marry free women who are not Kitābiyyah or Majūsiyyah, and they cannot marry slave women (even Muslims) because marriage to a slave woman is only allowed out of fear of fornication and lack of means, both of which are absent for prophets due to their infallibility and possession of wealth. The passage also notes that prophets may marry without a dowry. Finally, it derives from the statement that prophets do not have intercourse with their wives while they are fasting, in i‘tikāf, menstruating, in post-natal bleeding, or in iḥrām.

الحِل
الملك
النكاح
الأمة الكتابية
المجوسية
الوثنية
العنت
الطول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All forms of marriage are equally permissible for prophets.
Correction: The passage shows restrictions based on the woman's faith and status: prophets cannot marry Kitābiyyah, Majūsiyyah, or slave women.

Checkpoint

A) It is forbidden by consensus.
B) Because she is not free.
C) Because the reasons that permit marrying a slave (fear of fornication and lack of dowry) are absent for prophets.
D) Because it would lower his status.

Key Takeaway
Prophets' permissible relations are highly regulated, with specific conditions for ownership and marriage that emphasize their purity and special status.

Wet Dreams Are Impermissible for Prophets
Author rules that wet dreams are impermissible for prophets due to satanic origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why wet dreams are ruled impermissible for prophets and how a purely physical discharge is distinguished.

Core Idea
Wet dreams are from Satan, so prophets are protected from them.

In this passage, the author addresses a sensitive but important aspect of prophetic infallibility. Wet dreams are often misunderstood; here the author clarifies that they are not permitted for prophets because of their satanic origin. However, a purely physical discharge without satanic influence is not problematic. Fainting is mentioned but its ruling is deferred.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the concise style and the quoted hadith.
The author uses a strong assertion 'لا يجوز'.
2
Identify the ruling and evidence
Find the ruling on wet dreams and the two pieces of evidence: al-Nawawī's affirmation and the hadith. Understand the logical connection.
The hadith is quoted to reinforce the ruling.
3
Examine the exception
Note the exception for a mere flow of fluid without Satan's manipulation. Contrast this with the prohibited wet dream.
The distinction is based on the presence or absence of satanic involvement.
4
Reflect on prophetic protection
Consider why prophets are protected from satanic influence in such matters and how this aligns with their infallibility.
This connects to broader concepts of 'isma (protection from sin).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاحتلامُ والإغماء في حقِّ الرُّسل عليهمُ الصَّلاة والسَّلامُ ولا يجوز الاحتلام عليهم كما صحَّحه النووي ؛ لأنه من الشيطان، وقد ورد: «ما احتلم نبيٌّ قَطُّ» ، نعم إن كان مجرد فيضان ماء من غير تلاعب من الشيطان .. فلا مانع منه .

And it has been reported: 'No prophet ever had a wet dream.' Yes, if it is merely a flow of fluid without Satan's manipulation, then there is no harm in it.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on two conditions: wet dreams (iḥtilām) and fainting (ighmā') regarding prophets. The author first states that wet dreams are not permissible for prophets, citing al-Nawawī's affirmation, because wet dreams are caused by Satan. This is supported by a hadith that no prophet ever had a wet dream. However, the author makes a distinction: if it is merely a physical flow of fluid without any influence from Satan, then it is not harmful. This suggests that the prohibition is specifically tied to the satanic nature of the dream, not to the physical phenomenon itself. Fainting is mentioned in the title but not discussed here; it will be elaborated later.

Permissible Physical Afflictions for Prophets
Classification of permissible and impermissible physical afflictions for prophets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which physical afflictions are permissible for prophets and which are not, based on the criterion of not causing deficiency or repulsiveness.

Core Idea
Prophets may suffer illness but not defects that cause deficiency or repulsion.

This passage from the commentary on Jawharat al-Tawḥīd clarifies the boundaries of physical afflictions that prophets may experience. While ordinary human ailments like illness and brief fainting are allowed, conditions that imply deficiency or are repulsive are categorically excluded. The author provides scriptural evidence to support these distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English side by side to grasp the author's classification.
2
Identify permissible and impermissible conditions
List the conditions mentioned and note the reasoning for each. Pay attention to the condition on fainting.
3
Examine the historical examples
See how the author uses stories of prophets like Jacob, Job, and Shu'ayb to support the rule.
4
Understand the footnote about fainting
The footnote explains that fainting does not affect the heart's purity.
5
Reflect on the underlying principle
The key criterion is that afflictions must not cause deficiency or repulsion. This is a matter of prophetic dignity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومثل ما ذكره المصنف من الأكل والجماع سائر الأعراض البشرية، التي لا تُؤدي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العليَّة كالمرض، ومنه الإغماء فيجوز عليهم، وقيد أبو حامد الإغماء بغيرِ الطويل، وجزم به البلقيني بخلاف الجنون قليله وكثيره؛ لأنه نقص، وكالجنون: الجذام والبرص والعمى وغير ذلك من الأمور المنفّرة، فلم يَعْمَ نبي قط، ولم يثبت أن شعيباً كان ضريراً، وما كان بيعقوب فهو حجاب على العين من تواصل الدموع، ولذا لما جاءه البشير عاد بصيراً، وما كان بأيوب من البلاء فكان بين الجلد والعظم، فلم يكن منفّراً، وما اشتهر في القصَّة من الحكايات المنفرة فهي باطلة.
(١) قوله : (ومنه) ذكر المصنف صاحب المتن أن إغماءهم يستر ظواهرهم دون قلوبهم؛ لأن قلوبهم إذا عُصمت من النوم الذي هو أخف أختُ من الإغماء، فعِصمتُها من الإغماء بالطريق الأولى. انتهى أجهوري.
And similar to what the author mentioned of eating and intercourse are the rest of human attributes that do not lead to deficiency in their lofty ranks, such as illness, and among them is fainting, so it is permissible for them. Abū Ḥāmid (al-Ghazālī) restricted fainting to that which is not prolonged, and al-Bulqīnī affirmed it, contrary to madness, whether little or much, because it is deficiency. And like madness: leprosy, vitiligo, blindness, and other repulsive matters. Thus no prophet ever became blind, and it is not established that Shu‘ayb was blind. What happened to Jacob was a veil over his eyes from continuous tears, hence when the bearer of good news came, he regained sight. What afflicted Job was between skin and bone, so it was not repulsive. And what is commonly known in the story of repulsive tales are false. (Footnote) (1) His statement: 'and among them' – the author of the matn mentioned that their fainting covers their external bodies but not their hearts, because their hearts are protected from sleep, which is lighter than fainting, so their protection from fainting is even more so. End of al-Ajhūrī.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a classification of permissible and impermissible physical afflictions for prophets. It begins by stating that, like eating and intercourse, other human attributes that do not cause a deficiency in their exalted rank are permissible, such as illness. Among these, fainting (ighmā') is permissible, but with a condition: according to Abū Ḥāmid al-Ghazālī, it must not be prolonged; al-Bulqīnī affirmed this. In contrast, madness (junūn) is not permissible, whether little or much, because it is a deficiency. Similarly, leprosy (judhām), vitiligo (baraṣ), blindness (‘amā), and other repulsive conditions are also impermissible. The author then provides historical evidence: no prophet ever became blind; it is not established that Shu‘ayb was blind; Jacob's eye condition was due to continuous tears, not blindness; Job's affliction was internal (between skin and bone) and not repulsive. Popular repulsive tales about prophets are false. The footnote clarifies that fainting covers the prophets' external bodies but not their hearts, as their hearts are protected even from sleep, so they are certainly protected during fainting.

Key Terms
الجنون
الجذام
البرص
العمى
الإغماء
المنفِّرات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think any illness is permissible for prophets.
Correction: Only illnesses that do not cause deficiency or repulsiveness are allowed; madness and repulsive defects are prohibited.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is impermissible for prophets?
A) Illness
B) Fainting (if short)
C) Madness
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Prophets may experience non-repulsive human ailments like illness and short fainting, but they are protected from any condition that implies deficiency or repulsion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you were to face a prolonged illness or a condition that others find repulsive, would you still be able to maintain the same level of devotion and reliance on Allah as the prophets did? What steps can you take today to strengthen your faith for such trials?

Forgetfulness in Prophets: Sahw and Nisyān
Author explains the rules of forgetfulness in prophets, distinguishing between sahw and nisyān.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nuanced rulings on forgetfulness (sahw and nisyān) in prophets, including which types are impossible and which are permissible, and the rationale behind these distinctions.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from forgetfulness in conveying revelation, but not from all forms of forgetfulness.

This passage from Tuhfat al-Murīd presents a detailed classification of forgetfulness (sahw and nisyān) as it applies to prophets. It distinguishes between forgetfulness in conveying revelation—which is impossible—and forgetfulness in actions or after delivery, which may be permissible for legislative purposes. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for a correct theology of prophethood (ʿilm al-nubuwwa).

Guided Path
1
Distinguish sahw and nisyān
The passage uses two terms: sahw (unintentional oversight) and nisyān (forgetting). Note how each is treated separately. Underline the definitions.
Sahw is a momentary lapse, nisyān is a permanent forgetting.
2
Identify the ruling on sahw
Sahw is impossible for prophets in conveying reports (akhbār balāghiyya) but permissible in actions, especially for legislation. Find the example of forgetfulness in prayer.
The author emphasizes that their sahw does not arise from negligence.
3
Identify the ruling on nisyān
Nisyān is impossible before delivery of the message (whether verbal or practical), but permissible after delivery. Note the examples of forgetting a statement or a commanded prayer.
After delivering the message, forgetting the content is allowed.
4
Understand Satanic forgetfulness
The passage explicitly states that nisyān caused by Satan is impossible for prophets. Analyze the explanation of Yusha‘s statement and Adam's case.
This guards against misconceptions about prophetic infallibility.
5
Summarize the overall principle
The conclusion states that anything permissible for humans that does not lead to deficiency is permissible for prophets outwardly.
This provides a general rule for prophetic attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السهو والنسيان في حق الرُّسل عليهم الصَّلاة والسَّلامُ] وأما السهو فممتنع عليهم في الأخبار البلاغية، كقولهم : الجنَّة أعدت للمتقين وعذاب القبر واجب ... وهكذا، وغير البلاغية كـ (قام زيد، وقعد عمرو) ،وهكذا، وجائز عليهم في الأفعال البلاغية وغيرها كالسهو في الصلاة للتشريع، لكن ناشئاً لم يكن سهوهم عن اشتغالهم بغير ربهم، ولذلك قال بعضهم : [من البسيط] يَا سَائِلِي عَنْ رَسولِ اللهِ كَيْفَ سَهَا وَالسَّهْرُ مِنْ كُلِّ قَلْبٍ غَافِلٍ لَاءِ قَدْ غَابَ عَنْ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ سِرُّهُ فَسَها عَمَّا سِوَى اللَّهِ فَالتَّعْظِيمُ اللَّهِ ، وأما النسيان فهو ممتنع في البلاغيات قبل ،تبليغها قوليَّةً كانت أو فعليَّةٌ، فالقولية كالجنة أعدت للمتقين، والفعليَّةُ كصلاة الضحى إذا أمرهم الله بفعلها ليُقتدى بهم فيها .. فلا يجوز نسيان كل منهما قبل تبليغ الأولى بالقول والثانية بالفعل، وأما بعد التبليغ . . فيجوز نسيان ما ذكر من الله تعالى. وأما نسيان الشيطان فمستحيل عليهم، إذ ليس للشيطان عليهم سبيل، وقول يوشع : ﴿وَمَا أَنسَنِيهُ إِلَّا الشَّيْطَنُ ﴾ [الكهف: ٦٣] فتواضع منه، أو قبل نبوته وعلمه بحال نفسه وإلا فهو رحماني بشهادة وذلِكَ مَا كُنَّا نَبي ﴾ [الكهف: ٦٤] ، ووسوسة الشيطان لآدم بتمثيل ظاهري والممنوع لعبه ببواطنهم. وبالجملة فيجوز على ظواهرهم ما يجوز على البشر ممَّا لا يُؤدي إلى نقص،
Forgetfulness (sahw) and forgetfulness (nisyān) regarding the messengers (peace and blessings be upon them): As for forgetfulness (sahw), it is impossible for them in matters of conveying reports, like their saying 'Paradise is prepared for the pious' and 'Punishment of the grave is necessary' and so on. And in non-conveying matters like 'Zayd stood' and 'Amr sat', and so on. And it is permissible for them in conveying and other actions like forgetfulness in prayer for legislation, but their forgetfulness did not arise from preoccupation with other than their Lord. Hence some said: [in basīṭ meter] 'O asker about the Messenger of Allah how he forgot, while vigilance from every heedless heart...' (poem). And as for forgetfulness (nisyān), it is impossible in matters of conveying before delivery, whether in words or actions. Verbal like 'Paradise is prepared for the pious', and actions like the forenoon prayer if Allah commanded them to perform it to be followed, so forgetting either before delivering the first in words and the second in action is not permissible. After delivery, forgetting what was mentioned from Allah is permissible. As for forgetting from Satan, it is impossible for them, as Satan has no way over them. The statement of Yusha‘ 'And none made me forget it except Satan' (Sūrat al-Kahf: 63) is an act of humility from him, or before his prophethood and knowledge of his state, otherwise it is from the Merciful, as evidenced by 'That is what we were seeking' (al-Kahf: 64). And the whispering of Satan to Adam was through outward representation; what is forbidden is his play with their inner selves. In summary, it is permissible in their outward aspects what is permissible for humans that does not lead to deficiency.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on forgetfulness (sahw and nisyān) in prophets. It distinguishes two types: sahw (unintentional oversight) and nisyān (forgetting). For sahw, it is impossible for prophets in matters of conveying revelation (al-akhbār al-balāghiyyah) – both in words (e.g., stating paradise is for the pious) and in non-conveying statements (e.g., 'Zayd stood'). However, sahw is permissible in actions related to conveying or otherwise, such as forgetfulness in prayer for the purpose of legislation (tashrī‘). Importantly, their forgetfulness does not stem from negligence of God; a poem illustrates that their forgetfulness is due to their absorption in God. For nisyān, it is impossible in matters of conveying (al-balāghiyyāt) before they have delivered the message, whether verbal or practical. For example, forgetting a statement about paradise before saying it, or forgetting to perform a commanded prayer before demonstrating it. After delivering the message, forgetting the content is permissible. Forgetting caused by Satan is absolutely impossible, as Satan has no influence over them. The verse of Yusha‘ (Joshua) is explained as either humility or before prophethood. Finally, the passage summarizes that everything permissible for humans that does not cause deficiency is permissible for prophets outwardly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets never forget anything at all.
Correction: Prophets may forget after delivering the message or in legislative actions, but never before delivery nor due to Satan.

Checkpoint
In which situation is forgetfulness (nisyān) permissible for a prophet?
A) Before delivering a revelation
B) After delivering a revelation
C) In all matters of conveying
D) When caused by Satan

Key Takeaway
Prophets are protected from forgetfulness in conveying revelation but may experience it in actions for legislation or after delivery, and never from Satan.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you forget to perform a good deed or fall short in worship, do you immediately attribute it to Shaytan, or do you first examine whether your heart was preoccupied with worldly distractions? What does the Prophet's freedom from negligence teach you about the real source of your own lapses?
?
The Prophet's forgetfulness in prayer was a deliberate act from Allah to teach the Ummah. Think of a recent mistake you made that affected others. Could your error become a lesson for them? How can you shift from seeing your slip as a failure to seeing it as an opportunity for guidance?
?
Do you ever feel that your forgetfulness in religious matters is a sign of spiritual weakness? How does knowing that the Prophet, despite his perfection, experienced permissible forgetfulness—yet never from neglect of Allah—change your perspective on your own shortcomings? Are you more accountable for your distractions than you admit?

Permissible and Impermissible Physical Defects for Prophets
Classification of permissible and impermissible physical defects for prophets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which physical defects are permissible for prophets and which are not, and the reasoning behind these distinctions.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from repulsive defects but not from minor ailments.

This lesson examines the limits of prophetic infallibility regarding physical conditions. The commentator lists specific defects that are permissible, such as short fainting, and those that are not, like madness and blindness. By clarifying these boundaries, we learn the precise scope of prophetic protection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then its translation. Notice the flow from general rule to specific examples.
The passage uses a classification style.
2
Identify permissible and impermissible defects
List the defects mentioned: fainting (permissible with condition), madness (impermissible), leprosy, vitiligo, blindness (impermissible).
Fainting is allowed only if short.
3
Analyze the scriptural examples
Reflect on the cases of Shu'ayb (no blindness proven), Ya'qub (blindness from tears), and Ayyub (internal affliction). See how they illustrate the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النبوات 6 إلى نقص في مراتبهم العليَّة كالمرض، ومنه (١) الإغماء فيجوز عليهم، وقيد أبو حامد الإغماء بغيرِ الطويل، وجزم به البلقيني بخلاف الجنون قليله وكثيره؛ لأنه نقص، وكالجنون: الجذام والبرص والعمى وغير ذلك من الأمور المنفّرة، فلم يَعْمَ نبي قط، ولم يثبت أن شعيباً كان ضريراً، وما كان بيعقوب فهو حجاب على العين من تواصل الدموع، ولذا لما جاءه البشير عاد بصيراً، وما كان بأيوب من البلاء فكان بين الجلد والعظم، فلم يكن منفّراً، وما اشتهر في القصَّة من الحكايات المنفرة فهي باطلة.
(١) قوله : (ومنه) ذكر المصنف صاحب المتن أن إغماءهم يستر ظواهرهم دون قلوبهم؛ لأن قلوبهم إذا عُصمت من النوم الذي هو أخف أختُ من الإغماء، فعِصمتُها من الإغماء بالطريق الأولى. انتهى أجهوري.
Prophets 6: To deficiency in their high ranks like sickness, and from it is fainting, so it is permissible for them. Abu Hamid restricted fainting to that which is not prolonged, and al-Bulqini asserted it, contrary to madness, its little and its much, because it is a deficiency. And like madness: leprosy, vitiligo, blindness, and other repulsive things. So no prophet ever became blind, and it is not established that Shu'ayb was blind. And what was with Ya'qub was a veil over the eye from continuous tears, so when the bearer of good news came to him, he returned seeing. And what was with Ayyub of affliction was between the skin and the bone, so it was not repulsive. And what is famous in the story of repulsive tales are false. (1) His saying: 'And from it' – the author of the matn mentioned that their fainting conceals their outward appearances but not their hearts, because their hearts are protected from sleep which is lighter than fainting, so their protection from fainting is by primary inference. End of al-Ujhuri.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage discusses the extent of prophets' infallibility ('isma) regarding physical conditions. The commentator begins by affirming that some physical deficiencies are permissible for prophets, such as sickness and fainting, as long as they do not diminish their high status. He then refines this: Abu Hamid (al-Ghazali) restricts fainting to short periods, and al-Bulqini agrees. Madness, however, is absolutely impermissible for prophets because it is a clear deficiency. The commentator then lists other repulsive defects: leprosy, vitiligo, blindness, etc. He asserts that no prophet has ever been blind, and the apparent blindness of Shu'ayb is not proven. For Ya'qub, his blindness was due to tears, not a defect. For Ayyub, his affliction was internal (between skin and bone), not outwardly repulsive. The well-known repulsive stories are false. Finally, the footnote adds that fainting affects only their outward appearance, not their hearts, which are always connected to Allah, using an argument from the lesser to the greater: if hearts are protected from sleep (which is lighter), they are even more protected from fainting.

Key Terms
الإغماء
الجنون
الجذام
البرص
العمى
النبوة
العصمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets could be blind or have leprosy.
Correction: No, these are repulsive and prevented by prophetic infallibility.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following is permissible for prophets?
A) Madness
B) Leprosy
C) Short fainting
D) Blindness

Key Takeaway
Prophets may experience minor ailments like fainting, but they are protected from repulsive defects like blindness and madness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Allah protected His prophets from repulsive defects, yet you worry so much about your appearance. Are you more concerned with how others see you than with how Allah sees your heart? Will you today ask Allah to purify your inner state rather than your outer form?
?
The prophets suffered physical ailments like fainting and illness, yet they remained steadfast. When you face a minor sickness, do you complain and despair, forgetting that even the best of creation endured such trials? How will you change your response to your next illness?
?
Ya'qub's blindness was from excessive weeping for Yusuf—a sign of deep love for Allah's prophet. What are you crying over? Is it for the sake of Allah and His religion, or for worldly losses? Will you redirect your tears to what truly matters?

The Nature of Prophetic Fainting: Outward vs. Inward
Clarification of fainting's effect on prophets' hearts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophetic fainting affects only the outward appearance and not the heart, based on the argument from the lesser to the greater.

Core Idea
A prophet's heart remains connected to Allah even during fainting.

This short footnote clarifies a subtle point about prophetic fainting. It explains that fainting only conceals the prophets' outward state, while their hearts remain aware and protected. The reasoning uses the principle that if the heart is protected during sleep (which is lighter), it is even more protected during fainting.

Guided Path
1
Read the footnote text and translation
Carefully read the Arabic footnote and its translation. Note the key terms like 'isti'r' (concealing) and 'qalb' (heart).
2
Understand the argument from the lesser to the greater
The argument states that since the heart is protected from sleep (a lighter state), it is even more protected from fainting (a heavier state). Reflect on why sleep is considered lighter.
This is a logical inference (al-tariq al-ula).

Source Text

النبوات 6 إلى نقص في مراتبهم العليَّة كالمرض، ومنه (١) الإغماء فيجوز عليهم، وقيد أبو حامد الإغماء بغيرِ الطويل، وجزم به البلقيني بخلاف الجنون قليله وكثيره؛ لأنه نقص، وكالجنون: الجذام والبرص والعمى وغير ذلك من الأمور المنفّرة، فلم يَعْمَ نبي قط، ولم يثبت أن شعيباً كان ضريراً، وما كان بيعقوب فهو حجاب على العين من تواصل الدموع، ولذا لما جاءه البشير عاد بصيراً، وما كان بأيوب من البلاء فكان بين الجلد والعظم، فلم يكن منفّراً، وما اشتهر في القصَّة من الحكايات المنفرة فهي باطلة.
