Prophets and Forgetfulness: Distinguishing Types of Infallibility
Classification of sahw and nisyan for prophets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the types of forgetfulness (sahw and nisyan) that are permissible and impermissible for prophets, and the rationale behind these distinctions.

Core Idea
Prophets are infallible in delivering revelation but may experience minor forgetfulness in actions for legislative purposes.

This passage from the commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid provides a detailed classification of forgetfulness and forgetfulness in relation to prophets. It distinguishes between inadvertence in communicative reports versus actions, and between forgetfulness before and after delivering the message. Understanding these distinctions avoids misunderstandings about prophetic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read and distinguish sahw and nisyan
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note that sahw (inadvertence) and nisyan (forgetfulness) are treated separately. Pay attention to the different categories under each.
Sahw is about actions and reports; nisyan is about memory of revelation.
2
Analyze the classification of sahw
Identify that sahw is impossible in communicative reports (e.g., saying Paradise is for the pious) but permissible in actions (e.g., forgetfulness in prayer for legislation). Understand that this does not indicate negligence.
The poetic quote illustrates that the Prophet's forgetfulness was from being absorbed in Allah, not heedlessness.
3
Analyze the classification of nisyan
Note that nisyan of communicative matters (verbal or practical) is impossible before delivery, but permissible after delivery. Also, nisyan caused by Satan is absolutely impossible for prophets.
The verse about Yusha' is interpreted as humility or pre-prophethood.
4
Synthesize the broader principle
Reflect on the summary: prophets' outward actions follow human norms that do not cause deficiency, while their inner selves are always connected to Allah. The example of Ma'rūf al-Karkhī illustrates the high spiritual state of even followers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السهو والنسيان في حق الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام. وأما السهو فممتنع عليهم في الأخبار البلاغية، كقولهم : الجنَّة أعدت للمتقين وعذاب القبر واجب ... وهكذا، وغير البلاغية كـ (قام زيد، وقعد عمرو) ،وهكذا، وجائز عليهم في الأفعال البلاغية وغيرها كالسهو في الصلاة للتشريع، لكن ناشئاً لم يكن سهوهم عن اشتغالهم بغير ربهم، ولذلك قال بعضهم : [من البسيط] يَا سَائِلِي عَنْ رَسولِ اللهِ كَيْفَ سَهَا وَالسَّهْرُ مِنْ كُلِّ قَلْبٍ غَافِلٍ لَاءِ قَدْ غَابَ عَنْ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ سِرُّهُ فَسَها عَمَّا سِوَى اللَّهِ فَالتَّعْظِيمُ اللَّهِ. وأما النسيان فهو ممتنع في البلاغيات قبل تبليغها قوليَّةً كانت أو فعليَّةٌ، فالقولية كالجنة أعدت للمتقين، والفعليَّةُ كصلاة الضحى إذا أمرهم الله بفعلها ليُقتدى بهم فيها .. فلا يجوز نسيان كل منهما قبل تبليغ الأولى بالقول والثانية بالفعل، وأما بعد التبليغ . . فيجوز نسيان ما ذكر من الله تعالى. وأما نسيان الشيطان فمستحيل عليهم، إذ ليس للشيطان عليهم سبيل، وقول يوشع : ﴿وَمَا أَنسَانِيهُ إِلَّا الشَّيْطَانُ ﴾ [الكهف: ٦٣] فتواضع منه، أو قبل نبوته وعلمه بحال نفسه وإلا فهو رحماني بشهادة وَذَلِكَ مَا كُنَّا نَبي ﴾ [الكهف: ٦٤] ، ووسوسة الشيطان لآدم بتمثيل ظاهري والممنوع لعبه ببواطنهم. وبالجملة فيجوز على ظواهرهم ما يجوز على البشر ممَّا لا يُؤدي إلى نقص، وأما بواطنهم فمنزهةٌ عن ذلك، متعلّقة بربّهم، وفي المنن : كان معروف الكرخي يقول : (لي ثلاثون سنة في حضرة الله تعالى ما خرجت فأنا أكلم الله والناس يظنون أني أكلمهم انتهى. فإذا كان هذا حال أحد الأتباع، فما بالك بالأنبياء؟ خصوصاً رئيسهم الأعظم
Forgetfulness and forgetfulness (al-sahw wa al-nisyān) regarding the messengers, peace be upon them. As for forgetfulness (al-sahw), it is impossible for them in communicative reports (al-akhbār al-balāghiyya), like their saying: 'Paradise is prepared for the pious' and 'The punishment of the grave is obligatory'... etc. And in non-communicative matters like 'Zayd stood' and 'Amr sat', etc. And it is permissible for them in communicative and other actions, like forgetfulness in prayer for legislation, but it arises not from their preoccupation with other than their Lord. Therefore, some said: [al-basīt] O asker about the Messenger of Allah, how he forgot while wakefulness is from every heedless heart? He was absent from everything's secret, so he forgot other than Allah, so the magnification is for Allah. As for forgetfulness (al-nisyān), it is impossible in communicative matters before delivering them, whether verbal or practical. The verbal like 'Paradise is prepared for the pious', and the practical like the forenoon prayer if Allah commanded them to do it so that they may be followed in it... It is not permissible to forget each of them before delivering the first by speech and the second by action. And after delivery, it is permissible to forget what was mentioned from Allah. As for forgetfulness by Satan, it is impossible for them, for Satan has no path over them. And the saying of Yusha': {And none made me forget it except Satan} [al-Kahf 18:63] is humility from him, or before his prophethood and knowledge of his own state, otherwise it is from the Compassionate (raḥmānī) by the testimony {and that is what we were seeking} [al-Kahf 18:64]. And the whispering of Satan to Adam was by outward representation, and what is prevented is his playing with their inner selves. In sum, what is permissible for humans that does not lead to deficiency is permissible for their outward appearances, while their inner selves are pure from that, attached to their Lord. And in al-Minan: Ma'rūf al-Karkhī said: 'I have been for thirty years in the presence of Allah, I have not left, so I speak to Allah and people think I am speaking to them.' End. So if this is the state of a follower, what about the prophets? Especially their greatest leader.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of forgetfulness (sahw) and forgetfulness (nisyān) regarding prophets. The commentator begins by stating that sahw (inadvertence) is impossible for prophets in communicative reports (akhbār balāghiyya) which convey revelation, and also in ordinary statements (non-communicative) – meaning they do not inadvertently utter wrong words. However, sahw is permissible in actions, even in prayer, for the purpose of legislation (tashrī'), meaning to teach the community by forgetting part of the prayer. But this forgetfulness does not arise from negligence of their Lord; rather it is a divinely intended act. The commentator then quotes a poetic example. Next, nisyān (forgetfulness) is impossible for prophets before delivering the message, whether verbal or practical. After delivery, they may forget mundane things. Importantly, they are absolutely protected from forgetting due to Satan (nisyān al-shayṭān), as Satan has no power over them. The verse about Yusha' (Joshua) is interpreted as humility or pre-prophethood. Finally, the commentator summarizes that prophets' outward actions are subject to human norms that do not cause deficiency, but their inner selves are always connected to Allah, illustrated by the story of Ma'rūf al-Karkhī.

Key Terms
السهو
النسيان
الأخبار البلاغية
التبليغ
التشريع
الشيطان
العصمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets never forget anything, including after delivering the message.
Correction: The passage clarifies that prophets may forget mundane matters after delivering the message, but never forget revelation before or during delivery, and never due to Satan.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it permissible for a prophet to forget a matter of revelation?
A) Before delivering it to the community
B) After delivering it
C) Never
D) Only in dreams

Key Takeaway
Prophets are protected from forgetfulness that affects their message, but minor forgetfulness in actions is allowed for teaching purposes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have moments of forgetfulness in your worship—do you attribute them to a lack of focus on Allah, or do you admit that even your best efforts are imperfect? After studying how prophets forget for legislative wisdom, will you now view your own lapses as opportunities to learn humility and reliance on Allah, rather than excuses for carelessness?
?
The lesson says prophets' inner selves are always connected to Allah, even when their outward actions are subject to human norms. When you are speaking to people, how often is your inner self turned away from Allah? What would change if you strove to maintain that constant awareness of His presence, even in the midst of daily interactions?
?
If the greatest leader of the prophets (peace be upon him) experienced forgetfulness in acts of worship for the sake of teaching, how does that reshape your understanding of perfection in worship? Are you still striving for flawless outward performance, or are you more concerned with the sincerity and connection of your inner self to Allah?

The Inner Purity of Saints and Prophetic Infallibility
Discusses inner purity of saints and prophetic infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the inner purity of saints and the infallibility of prophets, including the scholarly consensus that prophets are protected from forgetfulness and error.

Core Idea
Saints are purified within, but prophets are infallible by divine protection.

This passage from the Tuhfat al-Mureed explores the spiritual states of saints and prophets. It begins by affirming the inner purity of saints, citing the profound example of Maruf al-Karkhi, and then elevates the discussion to the prophets, particularly their leader. The text then delves into the doctrine of prophetic infallibility ('isma), presenting scholarly views on what prophets are protected from, including forgetfulness, neglect, and error.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation to get the flow from saints to prophets.
Notice the contrast between 'their inner selves' and the prophetic discussion.
2
Understand the saint's example
Maruf al-Karkhi's statement illustrates constant awareness of God, a state of inner purity.
This is a high spiritual state, but not infallibility.
3
Consider the analogy to prophets
Reflect on the argument: if a follower can achieve such purity, how much more the prophets?
The analogy is used to elevate the discussion to prophetic infallibility.
4
Examine the infallibility views
Identify the two scholarly positions: one on forgetfulness/neglect (consensus), another including error.
The passage concludes that differences on details are not certain but opinions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما بواطنهم فمنزهةٌ عن ذلك، متعلّقة بربّهم، وفي المنن : كان معروف الكرخي يقول : (لي ثلاثون سنة في حضرة الله تعالى ما خرجت فأنا أكلم الله والناس يظنون أني أكلمهم) انتهى. فإذا كان هذا حال أحد الأتباع، فما بالك بالأنبياء؟ خصوصاً رئيسهم الأعظم (1) نصَّ القاضي عياض على الإجماع على امتناع السهو والنسيان في حقهم، والوارد مؤول، والأستاذ أبو إسحاق وتقي الدين السبكي على امتناع الخطأ والنسيان والسهو في حقهم. وكما قالوا : الاختلاف في هذه التفاصيل غير بالغ مبلغ القطع، بل هو من باب الظنون .
As for their inner selves, they are free from that, attached to their Lord. And in al-Minan: Maruf al-Karkhi used to say: 'I have been thirty years in the presence of Allah, the Exalted, not having left; I speak to Allah and people think I speak to them.' End. If this is the state of one of the followers, what about the prophets? Especially their greatest leader (1). Al-Qadi Iyad stated consensus on the impossibility of forgetfulness and oversight regarding them, and what is reported is interpreted. And al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq and Taqi al-Din al-Subki held the impossibility of error, forgetfulness, and oversight regarding them. And as they said: the difference in these details does not reach the level of certainty; rather it is from the realm of opinions.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage begins by describing the inner state of saints (awliya), asserting that their inner selves are pure and attached to God. It cites a saying of Maruf al-Karkhi, a famous saint, who claimed to be in constant awareness of God for thirty years. The author then argues by analogy: if a follower (tabi') can reach such a state, how much greater are the prophets, especially their leader Muhammad. The passage then addresses the issue of prophetic infallibility ('isma), citing al-Qadi Iyad's report of consensus (ijma') that prophets are protected from forgetfulness (sahu) and neglect (nisyan), and that any apparent contrary reports must be interpreted. Al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq and Taqi al-Din al-Subki are mentioned as holding the stronger view that error (khata'), forgetfulness, and neglect are all impossible for prophets. The passage concludes by noting that differences over these details do not constitute certainty but remain in the realm of opinion (zann).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That saints are infallible like prophets.
Correction: Saints are purified inwardly but are not protected from forgetfulness or error; only prophets have divine 'isma.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The passage teaches that while saints can attain inner purity, prophets are uniquely protected from forgetfulness, neglect, and error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If even a saint like Maruf al-Karkhi acknowledges that he is constantly speaking to God, do you truly live with that awareness, or do you often forget that you are always in His presence? What would change if you remembered this every moment?
?
The scholars affirm that prophets are protected from forgetfulness in conveying the message. Do you ever doubt or dismiss a prophetic teaching as if it were prone to error? How does this lesson call you to submit fully to the prophetic example, even when it challenges you?

The Second Testimony and the Three Rational Judgments for Prophets
Sanusi enumerates the three rational judgments for prophets and comments on the centrality of the two testimonies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the second testimony (Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah) entails the three rational judgments regarding prophets and why understanding the two testimonies is essential for faith.

Core Idea
The second shahada logically requires that prophets must be truthful, cannot lie, and may have permissible human traits.

This lesson unpacks the second part of the Islamic testimony of faith. The author shows that affirming the Prophet's message naturally leads to three categories of judgments about prophets: what is necessary, impossible, and possible for them to have. This logical structure is key to understanding prophethood in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice how the author derives the three categories from the second testimony.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the three rational judgments
Find the three categories listed: necessary attributes (truthfulness, trustworthiness, intelligence, conveying), impossible attributes (lying, betrayal, neglect, concealment), and permissible attributes (human accidents not implying deficiency).
These correspond to wājib, mustaḥīl, and jāʾiz.
3
Connect to the two testimonies
The passage concludes that the two testimonies together encompass all previous beliefs. Reflect on why the Lawgiver made these brief phrases the expression of faith.
This shows the comprehensiveness of the shahada.
4
Understand the importance of meaning
Scholars emphasize that one must understand the meaning of the testimonies, even in summary. Mere utterance without understanding is not beneficial.
This highlights the role of knowledge in faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجملة الثانية فيها الإقرار برسالته، ويلزم منه تصديقه في كل ما جاء به، ويندرج فيه وجوب صدق الرُّسل وأمانتهم وفطانتهم وتبليغهم لما أمروا بتبليغه للخلق، ويندرج فيه أيضاً استحالة الكذب والخيانة والغفلة والكتمان عليهم، ويندرج فيه أيضاً جوازُ جميع الأعراض البشرية التي لا تُؤدي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العليَّة، وهذه جملة أقسام الحكم العقلي الثلاثة المتعلقة بالرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام. فقد بان لك تضمن كلمتي الشهادة لجميع العقائد المتقدّمة، ولعلهما لهذا المعنى مع اختصارهما جعلهما الشارع ترجمة عمَّا في القلب من الإيمان، ولم يقبل من أحدٍ الإيمان إلا بهما مع القدرة عليهما، وقد نصَّ العلماء على أنه لا بد من فهم معناهما ولو إجمالاً، وإلا لم ينتفع الناطق بهما. وقال بعضهم : الأوسع للذاكر أن يلاحظ أخذهما من القرآن ليثاب عليهما مطلقاً.
And the second sentence contains the affirmation of his message, and from it follows believing him in everything he came with, and includes in it the necessity of the truthfulness of the messengers, their trustworthiness, their intelligence, and their conveying what they were commanded to convey to creation, and includes in it also the impossibility of lying, betrayal, neglect, and concealment upon them, and includes in it also the permissibility of all human accidents that do not lead to deficiency in their lofty ranks. And this is the summary of the three divisions of rational judgment pertaining to the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them. So it has become clear to you that the two words of the testimony encompass all the preceding beliefs, and perhaps it is for this meaning, despite their brevity, that the Lawgiver made them the expression of what is in the heart of faith, and did not accept faith from anyone except through them when able to utter them. And the scholars have stated that understanding their meaning, even if in summary, is necessary, otherwise the speaker does not benefit from them. And some said: the most rewarding for the one who remembers is to observe that he takes them from the Qur'an so that he may be rewarded for them absolutely.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage explains the implications of the second testimony (محمد رسول الله). The author begins: the second testimony affirms the message of the Prophet, and from that it necessarily follows (يلزم) that one must believe everything the Prophet brought. From this, three categories of rational judgment regarding the prophets are derived:

1. Necessary (واجب): Prophets must be truthful (صدق), trustworthy (أمانة), intelligent (فطانة), and must convey (تبليغ) what they were commanded to convey.
2. Impossible (مستحيل): The opposites are impossible: lying (كذب), betrayal (خيانة), neglect (غفلة), and concealment (كتمان).
3. Possible (جائز): Any human accidents (أعراض بشرية) that do not detract from their high rank are permissible for them. This includes things like eating, sleeping, marriage, etc., as long as they do not imply a deficiency.

The author then concludes that the two testimonies together encompass all the beliefs discussed earlier. He notes that this is why the Lawgiver (الشارع) made these two phrases the declaration of faith despite their brevity, and faith is not accepted without them when one is able to utter them. Scholars have emphasized the necessity of understanding their meaning, even in summary; otherwise, mere utterance is worthless.

The passage ends with a note from some scholars that the most rewarding way to recite them is to intend that one is taking them from the Quran, thus gaining reward for reciting Quranic verses.

الرسالة
الصدق
الأمانة
الفطانة
التبليغ
الأعراض البشرية
الحكم العقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That prophets are free from all human experiences.
Correction: Prophets may experience permissible human traits (like eating, sleeping) as long as they do not imply deficiency.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an impossible attribute for prophets according to the passage?
A) Truthfulness
B) Intelligence
C) Lying
D) Conveying the message

Key Takeaway
The second testimony logically entails that prophets must be truthful, cannot lie, and may have permissible human traits, and understanding the two testimonies is essential for faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The scholars say understanding the shahada is necessary for it to benefit you. Have you ever said it without pausing to reflect on its meaning? What will you do today to ensure your tongue and heart are aligned?
?
If you truly believed that the Prophet cannot lie, how would that change the way you respond to a hadith that challenges your lifestyle? Are you willing to obey without hesitation starting now?

The Three Rational Judgments Concerning Prophets
Author outlines necessary, impossible, and possible attributes for prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of rational judgments (necessary, impossible, possible) as they apply to prophets, and why affirming a messenger necessitates these attributes.

Core Idea
Prophets must be truthful, trustworthy, intelligent, and convey the message; opposite traits are impossible; human traits are permissible if not demeaning.

This passage from Sanusi's Jawharah explains the logical implications of affirming a messenger. If we accept that someone is a true prophet, we must also accept certain attributes as necessary, others as impossible, and some as permissible. This framework is essential for understanding Islamic theology of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's concise style.
2
Identify the three categories
Look for the three rational judgments: necessary (wajib), impossible (mustahil), and possible (ja'iz). Note the specific attributes listed under each.
The passage uses 'yandariju fīhi' to introduce each category.
3
Reflect on the logic
Ask yourself why affirming a messenger logically requires these attributes. How does the concept of prophethood imply truthfulness, trustworthiness, intelligence, and conveyance?
This connects to the broader principle that a messenger must be credible and capable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجملة الثانية فيها الإقرار برسالته ، ويلزم منه تصديقه في كل ما جاء به، ويندرج فيه وجوب صدق الرُّسل وأمانتهم وفطانتهم وتبليغهم لما أمروا بتبليغه للخلق، ويندرج فيه أيضاً استحالة الكذب والخيانة والغفلة والكتمان عليهم، ويندرج فيه أيضاً جوازُ جميع الأعراض البشرية التي لا تُؤدي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العليَّة، وهذه جملة أقسام الحكم العقلي الثلاثة المتعلقة بالرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام.

And it also includes the impossibility of lying, treachery, heedlessness, and concealment upon them. Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage presents the second summary (al-jumla al-thaniya) concerning prophets. It begins by stating that affirming the messenger entails believing everything he brought. From this, the author deduces three categories of rational judgments for prophets: necessary (wajib) attributes—truthfulness (sidq), trustworthiness (amana), intelligence (fatana), and conveying what they were commanded; impossible (mustahil) attributes—lying (kadhib), treachery (khiyana), heedlessness (ghafla), and concealment (kitman); and possible (ja'iz) attributes—any human traits that do not detract from their lofty station. The passage concludes that this constitutes the three rational judgments regarding prophets.

Prophethood: Divine Selection, Not Human Acquisition
Ibn al-Mubarak explains that prophethood is a divine gift, not acquired.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Islamic theology insists that prophethood is a divine gift and not something that can be achieved through human effort, and how this differs from the philosophical view.

Core Idea
Prophethood is bestowed by Allah alone — no human effort can earn it.

This lesson examines a foundational doctrine in Islamic theology: prophethood is not a station that can be earned through spiritual practices. The poem states this clearly, and the commentary unpacks the disagreement with the philosophers about the very definition of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the poetic line and its explanation
Start by reading the Arabic line and its simple explanation. Notice the strong negation: 'no prophethood was acquired.' The author immediately clarifies that this means the servant cannot acquire it through specific causes like seclusion and worship.
2
Compare the Muslim and philosophical definitions
The passage presents two rival definitions: Muslims define prophethood as divine selection for receiving revelation, while philosophers see it as an acquired state of soul purity. Notice how each definition leads to a different conclusion about whether prophethood can be earned.
The disagreement is not just about a fact but about the very meaning of prophethood.
3
Grasp the consequence: finality of prophethood
The author argues that if prophethood could be acquired, it could theoretically be acquired after Prophet Muhammad, contradicting the Quranic verse 'the seal of the prophets' (Al-Ahzab:40). This is why the philosophical view is considered disbelief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النبوة اصطفاء لا اكتساب]
٦٣ - وَلَمْ تَكُنْ نُبُوَّةٌ مُكْتَسَبَهُ وَلَو رَقَى فِي الخَيْرِ أَعْلَى عَقَبَهُ 
قوله : (وَلَمْ تَكُنْ نُبُوَّةٌ مُكْتَسَبَه :أي: لا يكتسبها العبد بمباشرة أسباب مخصوصة، (۱)؛ كملازمة الخلوة والعبادة وتناول الحلال كما زعمت الفلاسفة لعنهم الله تعالى فالذي ذهب إليه المسلمون جميعاً أن النبوة خصيصة من الله تعالى، لا يبلغ العبد أن يكتسبها، ويفسرونها باختصاص العبد بسماع وحي من الله تعالى بحكم شرعي تكليفي، سواء أمر بتبليغه أم لا وهكذا ،الرسالة لكن بشرط أن يؤمر بالتبليغ. وذهبت الفلاسفة إلى أن النبوة مكتسبة للعبد بمباشرة أسباب خاصة، ويفسرونها بأنها صفاء وتجلُّ للنفس يحدث لها من الرياضات بالتخلي عن الأمور الذميمة، والتخلق بالأخلاق الحميدة، فالخلاف بين المسلمين والفلاسفة في أن النبوة ليست مكتسبة، أو أنها مُكتسبة .. مبني على الخلاف بينهما في معناها (۲)، والقول باكتساب النبوة أقوى المسائل التي كفرت بها الفلاسفة وإن لم تكن من المسائل المذكورة في النظم المشهور ويلزم على قولهم باكتسابها تجويز نبي بعد سيدنا مُحمَّدٍ أو معه، وذلك مُستلزم لتكذيب القرآن والسنة، فقد قال تعالى : ﴿وَخَاتَمَ النَّحْنُ ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٤٠]
(۱) إنما قال الفلاسفة بأن النبوة مكتسبة ؛ لأن المعجزة عندهم مكتسبة ؛ فهي إما صفاء نفس يؤدي إلى انطباع ما في اللوح المحفوظ ومعرفة الغيوب، أو فطنة بمعرفة النتائج بسرعة فائقة، أو التوهم للأشياء للنفس القوية، فتتأثر بها الطبيعيات وتتسخّر، ولكنها بهذا المعنى عندهم محدودة جدا، فلا تصل إلى قلب أعيان الأشياء، بل كتسيير الهواء مثلاً .
(۲) نقل العلامة الحافظ الشامي في سبل الهدى والرشاد عن الآمدي فقال: (وقال الآمدي رحمه الله تعالى - بعد حكايته مذهب الفلاسفة في النبوّة، وقول من قال : إن النبي من علم كونه نبيًّا، وقول من قال : إن النبوة سفارة بين الحق والخلق، وتزييف كل منها - : والحقُّ ما ذهب إليه أهلُ الحقِّ من الأشاعرة وغيرهم، من أن النبوة ليست راجعة إلى ذاتي من ذاتيات النبي، ولا إلى عرض من أعراضه المكتسبة له ، بل هى موهبة من الله تعالى ونعمةٌ منه عليه تجعله متأملاً للرسالة، وحاصلها يرجع إلى قول الله تعالى لمن اصطفاه من عباده أرسلتك أو بعثتك، فبلغ عني . انتهى . : فعلم بذلك : أن النبوة والرسالة من الصفات الاعتبارية ؛ كالولاية للولي ، والإمامة للسلطان، ونحو ذلك ؛ لأن القول لا يوجب لمتعلَّقِهِ صفةٌ كما صرح به القاضي عضد الدين).
[Prophethood is selection, not acquisition]
63. "And no prophethood was acquired, even if one rises in goodness to its highest peak."
His saying: "And no prophethood was acquired" means: the servant does not acquire it by undertaking specific causes, such as adhering to seclusion, worship, and consuming lawful food, as the philosophers claimed, may Allah curse them. For what all Muslims have held is that prophethood is a special characteristic from Allah, Most High, which the servant cannot attain by acquisition. They interpret it as the servant being singled out for hearing revelation from Allah, Most High, concerning a legally obligating ruling, whether he is commanded to convey it or not. And similarly for messengership (al-risāla), but with the condition that he is commanded to convey. The philosophers held that prophethood is acquired by the servant through undertaking special causes, and they interpret it as purity and manifestation for the soul that occurs from spiritual exercises by abandoning blameworthy matters and adopting praiseworthy morals. So the disagreement between Muslims and philosophers—whether prophethood is not acquired or is acquired—is based on their disagreement about its meaning. And the statement that prophethood is acquired is among the strongest matters for which the philosophers are declared disbelievers, even if it is not among the issues mentioned in the well-known list. And their saying that it is acquired entails permitting a prophet after our master Muhammad or with him, and that necessitates denying the Qur'an and the Sunnah. For He, Most High, said: "And the seal of the prophets" [Al-Ahzab: 40].
(1) The philosophers only said that prophethood is acquired because the miracle (al-mu'jiza) is acquired according to them. For it is either purity of soul that leads to imprinting what is in the Preserved Tablet and knowledge of unseen things, or sharpness in knowing results with extreme speed, or imagination of things for a strong soul, so natural things are affected by it and are subjugated. But in this sense, it is very limited according to them, not reaching the transformation of the essences of things, but like moving the air, for example.
(2) The scholar al-Hafiz al-Shami in Subul al-Huda wa al-Rashad narrated from al-Amidi, who said: (Al-Amidi, may Allah have mercy on him, after relating the philosophers' doctrine on prophethood, and the saying of those who said that the prophet is one who knows himself to be a prophet, and the saying of those who said that prophethood is an embassy between the Truth and creation, and falsifying each of them, said: The truth is what the people of truth among the Ash'aris and others have held, that prophethood is not reducible to an essential property of the prophet's essence, nor to an accident acquired by him, but rather it is a gift from Allah, Most High, and a favor from Him upon him that makes him prepared for the message. Its outcome goes back to the saying of Allah, Most High, to whomever He chooses from His servants: 'I have sent you' or 'I have raised you, so convey from Me.' End quote. So it is known by that that prophethood and messengership are from the attributive qualities (al-sifāt al-i'tibāriyya), like governance (al-wilāya) for the saint, and imamate for the ruler, and the like, because the saying does not cause a quality for its object, as al-Qadi 'Adud al-Din stated.)
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument establishing that prophethood is a divine selection, not an acquirable state. The author begins by quoting a poetic line: 'And no prophethood was acquired, even if one rises in goodness to its highest peak.' He then explains that the servant cannot acquire prophethood by performing specific practices like seclusion, worship, and eating lawful food, contrary to the claim of the philosophers (the falāsifa). All Muslims agree that prophethood is a special gift (khuṣūṣiyya) from Allah that the servant cannot attain through effort. Muslims define prophethood as the servant being singled out to hear divine revelation concerning a legally obligating rule, whether or not he is commanded to convey it; messengership adds the command to convey. The philosophers define it differently: as a purity and manifestation of the soul achieved through spiritual exercises and moral refinement. Thus the disagreement is based on different definitions. The author notes that declaring one a disbeliever for claiming prophethood is acquirable is one of the strongest matters for takfīr, even if not in the standard list. This is because believing prophethood is acquirable implies it could occur after or alongside Prophet Muhammad, which contradicts the Qur'anic verse 'the seal of the prophets' (Al-Ahzab:40), denying the finality of prophethood.

The first footnote elaborates on the philosophers' reasoning: they believe miracles are acquired through soul purity, intellectual sharpness, or strong imagination that influences natural phenomena. The second footnote quotes al-Āmidī who affirms the Ash'ari position that prophethood is not an essential property or acquired accident but a divine gift (mawhiba) and a favor, making the chosen servant prepared for the message. It is an attributive quality (ṣifa i'tibāriyya) like saintship and imamate—a relational status rather than an intrinsic attribute.

Key Terms
النبوة
المكتسبة
الفلسفة
الوحي
الحكم التكليفي
الرسالة
خاتم النّبيّين
الصفات الاعتبارية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That prophethood can be attained through extreme asceticism, spiritual exercises, or moral purification.
Correction: Prophethood is a divine gift (khuṣūṣiyya) from Allah, not an acquired state. No human effort can earn it; it is solely by Allah's choice.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the fundamental difference between Muslims and philosophers regarding prophethood?
A) Muslims believe prophethood is a divine gift; philosophers believe it is an acquired state.
B) Muslims believe prophethood is limited to the past; philosophers believe it can continue.
C) Muslims believe prophethood requires miracles; philosophers do not.
D) Muslims believe prophethood is only for Arabs; philosophers believe it is for all.

Key Takeaway
Prophethood is a divine selection, not a human achievement; to claim otherwise denies the finality of prophethood in Muhammad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever, even for a moment, felt that your acts of worship or spiritual discipline have earned you a status with Allah, forgetting that even prophethood is entirely His gift? How does this passage reorient your heart regarding divine favor?
?
This lesson refutes the idea that prophethood could be achieved through human effort. In your own life, where do you still trust your own striving over Allah's choice? What would it look like to fully accept that every good thing comes from Him alone?
?
If prophethood is a divine gift and not an earned status, then the Prophet's rank is purely by Allah's grace. Does your love and reverence for the Prophet reflect this truth, or is it entangled with a sense of human achievement? Commit to thanking Allah for this gift today.

The Muslim and Philosopher Definitions of Prophethood
Contrasting Muslim and philosophical definitions of prophethood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fundamental difference between the Muslim and philosophical definitions of prophethood and why the disagreement is rooted in their respective meanings.

Core Idea
Prophethood is a divine gift, not a human achievement.

In this passage, the commentator explains the line 'And prophethood was not acquired' by clarifying what Muslims believe about prophethood versus what the philosophers claimed. The disagreement is not merely verbal but stems from two completely different understandings of what prophethood actually is. Let's examine both definitions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic and its literal translation to get the main ideas.
Pay attention to the contrasting language.
2
Identify the two definitions
Notice how the commentator presents the Muslim definition first, then the philosophers' definition. Mark the key phrases.
Muslim definition: 'special gift', philosopher definition: 'purity and illumination'.
3
Understand the root of disagreement
The passage states that the conflict is based on the difference in meaning. Ask yourself: how do the two definitions differ in essence?
One is divine selection, the other is human effort.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَلَمْ تَكُنْ نُبُوَّةٌ مُكْتَسَبَه :أي: لا يكتسبها العبد بمباشرة أسباب مخصوصة، كملازمة الخلوة والعبادة وتناول الحلال كما زعمت الفلاسفة لعنهم الله تعالى فالذي ذهب إليه المسلمون جميعاً أن النبوة خصيصة من الله تعالى، لا يبلغ العبد أن يكتسبها، ويفسرونها باختصاص العبد بسماع وحي من الله تعالى بحكم شرعي تكليفي، سواء أمر بتبليغه أم لا وهكذا ،الرسالة لكن بشرط أن يؤمر بالتبليغ. وذهبت الفلاسفة إلى أن النبوة مكتسبة للعبد بمباشرة أسباب خاصة، ويفسرونها بأنها صفاء وتجلُّ للنفس يحدث لها من الرياضات بالتخلي عن الأمور الذميمة، والتخلق بالأخلاق الحميدة، فالخلاف بين المسلمين والفلاسفة في أن النبوة ليست مكتسبة، أو أنها مُكتسبة .. مبني على الخلاف بينهما في معناها (۱)، والقول باكتساب النبوة أقوى المسائل التي كفرت بها الفلاسفة وإن لم تكن من المسائل المذكورة في النظم المشهور ويلزم على قولهم باكتسابها تجويز نبي بعد سيدنا مُحمَّدٍ أو معه، وذلك مُستلزم لتكذيب القرآن والسنة، فقد قال تعالى : ﴿وَخَاتَمَ النَّحْنُ ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٤٠] وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: لا نبي بعدي» (۱) ، وأجمعت الأمة على إبقائه على ظاهره. (۱) إنما قال الفلاسفة بأن النبوة مكتسبة ؛ لأن المعجزة عندهم مكتسبة ؛ فهي إما صفاء نفس يؤدي إلى انطباع ما في اللوح المحفوظ ومعرفة الغيوب، أو فطنة بمعرفة النتائج بسرعة فائقة، أو التوهم للأشياء للنفس القوية، فتتأثر بها الطبيعيات وتتسخّر، ولكنها بهذا المعنى عندهم محدودة جدا، فلا تصل إلى قلب أعيان الأشياء، بل كتسيير الهواء مثلاً . (۲) نقل العلامة الحافظ الشامي في سبل الهدى والرشاد عن الآمدي فقال: (وقال الآمدي رحمه الله تعالى - بعد حكايته مذهب الفلاسفة في النبوّة، وقول من قال : إن النبي من علم كونه نبيًّا، وقول من قال : إن النبوة سفارة بين الحق والخلق، وتزييف كل منها - : والحقُّ ما ذهب إليه أهلُ الحقِّ من الأشاعرة وغيرهم، من أن النبوة ليست راجعة إلى ذاتي من ذاتيات النبي، ولا إلى عرض من أعراضه المكتسبة له ، بل هى موهبة من الله تعالى ونعمةٌ منه عليه تجعله متأملاً للرسالة، وحاصلها يرجع إلى قول الله تعالى لمن اصطفاه من عباده أرسلتك أو بعثتك، فبلغ عني . انتهى . : فعلم بذلك : أن النبوة والرسالة من الصفات الاعتبارية ؛ كالولاية للولي ، والإمامة للسلطان، ونحو ذلك ؛ لأن القول لا يوجب لمتعلَّقِهِ صفةٌ كما صرح به القاضي عضد الدين).
His saying: (And prophethood was not acquired) means: The servant does not acquire it by directly engaging in specific causes, such as adhering to seclusion, worship, and consuming lawful things as the philosophers – may Allah curse them – claimed. Rather, all Muslims hold that prophethood is a special gift from Allah, the servant cannot acquire it. They interpret it as the servant being singled out to hear revelation from Allah concerning a shar'i obligating ruling, whether he is commanded to convey it or not, and likewise with messengership, but with the condition that he is commanded to convey. The philosophers held that prophethood is acquired by the servant through directly engaging in specific causes, and they interpret it as a purity and illumination of the soul that occurs to him through spiritual exercises by abandoning blameworthy matters and adopting praiseworthy morals. So the disagreement between Muslims and philosophers on whether prophethood is not acquired or that it is acquired is based on their disagreement about its meaning. The statement that prophethood is acquired is among the gravest matters for which the philosophers were deemed disbelievers, even if it is not among the matters mentioned in the well-known poem. And necessary upon their claim of its acquisition is permitting a prophet after our master Muhammad or with him, and that entails denying the Quran and the Sunnah. Allah said: {and the seal of the prophets} [Al-Ahzab: 40] and he, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'There is no prophet after me,' and the community agreed to take it at face value. (1) The philosophers only said that prophethood is acquired because, in their view, the miracle is acquired. So it is either a purity of soul that leads to imprinting of what is in the Preserved Tablet and knowledge of the unseen, or a perspicacity in knowing outcomes with extreme speed, or the imagination of things for the powerful soul, so that natural things are affected by it and are subjected. But in this sense, according to them, it is very limited, so it does not reach the point of transforming the very essences of things, but rather like moving the air, for example. (2) The scholar al-Hafiz al-Shami in 'Subul al-Huda wa al-Rashad' transmitted from al-Amidi who said: (After al-Amidi related the philosophers' doctrine on prophethood, and the saying of those who say that the prophet knows himself to be a prophet, and the saying of those who say that prophethood is an embassy between the Truth and creation, and he refuted each, he said: The truth is what the people of truth among the Ash'aris and others have held, that prophethood is not reducible to an essential attribute of the prophet's essence, nor to an acquired accident of his, but it is a gift from Allah and a favor from Him upon him that makes him reflect on messengership. Its net result is that Allah says to whom He chooses from His servants: 'I have sent you' or 'I have commissioned you, so convey from Me.' End quote.) Thus it is known that prophethood and messengership are relational attributes (al-sifaat al-i'tibariyya), like sainthood for the saint and imamate for the sultan, and so on; because speech does not necessitate an attribute for its object, as Qadi 'Adud al-Din stated.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary on the line 'And prophethood was not acquired.' It begins by defining the Muslim position: the servant does not acquire prophethood by any specific actions or practices, contrary to the philosophers. The author explains that Muslims interpret prophethood as a special divine gift whereby the servant receives revelation of a legal ruling, whether or not he is commanded to convey it; messengership adds the condition of conveyance. The philosophers, however, view prophethood as acquired through spiritual exercises that purify the soul. The disagreement is rooted in differing definitions. The author then states that the philosophers' claim of acquisition is one of the strongest grounds for declaring them disbelievers, even if not explicitly mentioned in the famous poem. He then argues that their view necessarily allows for the possibility of a prophet after Muhammad, which contradicts the Quran (Ahzab:40) and the hadith 'There is no prophet after me,' and the consensus of the community. The passage includes two footnotes: the first explains the philosophers' view that miracles are acquired, limited to certain effects; the second transmits al-Amidi's position that prophethood is not an essential attribute or acquired accident but a divine gift, making it a relational attribute (sifa i'tibariyya) similar to sainthood or imamate, since the divine address does not create a real attribute in the person. The conclusion clarifies that prophethood and messengership are such attributes.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The passage clarifies that Muslims unanimously hold it is a divine gift, not acquired.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The philosophers believed they could achieve prophethood through their own efforts. Where in your spiritual life do you subtly rely on your own actions rather than Allah's grace, and how does this lesson challenge that reliance?
?
Prophethood is a divine gift, not earned. Does your heart truly accept that you can never 'earn' Allah's favor by your deeds alone, or do you still feel entitled to His rewards? What would change if you fully lived in that dependency?
?
If every prophet was chosen by Allah without any prior merit, how does that reshape your relationship with the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ? Are you grateful for his prophethood as a sheer gift, or do you take it for granted?

Refuting the Philosophers and the True Nature of Prophethood
Refutation of acquired prophethood and definition of prophethood as a relational attribute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the philosophers' view on prophethood is considered disbelief and how prophethood is a relational attribute, not an essential quality.

Core Idea
Claiming prophethood is acquired leads to denying the finality of prophethood.

After establishing the definitions, the commentator now delivers the decisive refutation. He argues that the philosophers' claim necessarily implies the possibility of prophets after Muhammad, which contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus. Moreover, he clarifies that prophethood is not an inherent quality but a relational attribute conferred by Allah's address.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully, noting the refutation and the quote from al-Amidi.
The passage includes footnotes that explain the philosophers' view on miracles and the Ash'ari position.
2
Analyze the logical consequence
The commentator says that if prophethood is acquired, then a prophet could appear after or with Muhammad. How does this lead to disbelief?
It contradicts explicit Quranic and hadith texts and consensus.
3
Understand the conclusion about prophethood's nature
The quote from al-Amidi defines prophethood as a relational attribute. Compare this to the philosophers' view.
A relational attribute does not change the essence, unlike acquired traits.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَلَمْ تَكُنْ نُبُوَّةٌ مُكْتَسَبَه :أي: لا يكتسبها العبد بمباشرة أسباب مخصوصة، كملازمة الخلوة والعبادة وتناول الحلال كما زعمت الفلاسفة لعنهم الله تعالى فالذي ذهب إليه المسلمون جميعاً أن النبوة خصيصة من الله تعالى، لا يبلغ العبد أن يكتسبها، ويفسرونها باختصاص العبد بسماع وحي من الله تعالى بحكم شرعي تكليفي، سواء أمر بتبليغه أم لا وهكذا ،الرسالة لكن بشرط أن يؤمر بالتبليغ. وذهبت الفلاسفة إلى أن النبوة مكتسبة للعبد بمباشرة أسباب خاصة، ويفسرونها بأنها صفاء وتجلُّ للنفس يحدث لها من الرياضات بالتخلي عن الأمور الذميمة، والتخلق بالأخلاق الحميدة، فالخلاف بين المسلمين والفلاسفة في أن النبوة ليست مكتسبة، أو أنها مُكتسبة .. مبني على الخلاف بينهما في معناها (۱)، والقول باكتساب النبوة أقوى المسائل التي كفرت بها الفلاسفة وإن لم تكن من المسائل المذكورة في النظم المشهور ويلزم على قولهم باكتسابها تجويز نبي بعد سيدنا مُحمَّدٍ أو معه، وذلك مُستلزم لتكذيب القرآن والسنة، فقد قال تعالى : ﴿وَخَاتَمَ النَّحْنُ ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٤٠] وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: لا نبي بعدي» (۱) ، وأجمعت الأمة على إبقائه على ظاهره. (۱) إنما قال الفلاسفة بأن النبوة مكتسبة ؛ لأن المعجزة عندهم مكتسبة ؛ فهي إما صفاء نفس يؤدي إلى انطباع ما في اللوح المحفوظ ومعرفة الغيوب، أو فطنة بمعرفة النتائج بسرعة فائقة، أو التوهم للأشياء للنفس القوية، فتتأثر بها الطبيعيات وتتسخّر، ولكنها بهذا المعنى عندهم محدودة جدا، فلا تصل إلى قلب أعيان الأشياء، بل كتسيير الهواء مثلاً . (۲) نقل العلامة الحافظ الشامي في سبل الهدى والرشاد عن الآمدي فقال: (وقال الآمدي رحمه الله تعالى - بعد حكايته مذهب الفلاسفة في النبوّة، وقول من قال : إن النبي من علم كونه نبيًّا، وقول من قال : إن النبوة سفارة بين الحق والخلق، وتزييف كل منها - : والحقُّ ما ذهب إليه أهلُ الحقِّ من الأشاعرة وغيرهم، من أن النبوة ليست راجعة إلى ذاتي من ذاتيات النبي، ولا إلى عرض من أعراضه المكتسبة له ، بل هى موهبة من الله تعالى ونعمةٌ منه عليه تجعله متأملاً للرسالة، وحاصلها يرجع إلى قول الله تعالى لمن اصطفاه من عباده أرسلتك أو بعثتك، فبلغ عني . انتهى . : فعلم بذلك : أن النبوة والرسالة من الصفات الاعتبارية ؛ كالولاية للولي ، والإمامة للسلطان، ونحو ذلك ؛ لأن القول لا يوجب لمتعلَّقِهِ صفةٌ كما صرح به القاضي عضد الدين).
His saying: (And prophethood was not acquired) means: The servant does not acquire it by directly engaging in specific causes, such as adhering to seclusion, worship, and consuming lawful things as the philosophers – may Allah curse them – claimed. Rather, all Muslims hold that prophethood is a special gift from Allah, the servant cannot acquire it. They interpret it as the servant being singled out to hear revelation from Allah concerning a shar'i obligating ruling, whether he is commanded to convey it or not, and likewise with messengership, but with the condition that he is commanded to convey. The philosophers held that prophethood is acquired by the servant through directly engaging in specific causes, and they interpret it as a purity and illumination of the soul that occurs to him through spiritual exercises by abandoning blameworthy matters and adopting praiseworthy morals. So the disagreement between Muslims and philosophers on whether prophethood is not acquired or that it is acquired is based on their disagreement about its meaning. The statement that prophethood is acquired is among the gravest matters for which the philosophers were deemed disbelievers, even if it is not among the matters mentioned in the well-known poem. And necessary upon their claim of its acquisition is permitting a prophet after our master Muhammad or with him, and that entails denying the Quran and the Sunnah. Allah said: {and the seal of the prophets} [Al-Ahzab: 40] and he, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'There is no prophet after me,' and the community agreed to take it at face value. (1) The philosophers only said that prophethood is acquired because, in their view, the miracle is acquired. So it is either a purity of soul that leads to imprinting of what is in the Preserved Tablet and knowledge of the unseen, or a perspicacity in knowing outcomes with extreme speed, or the imagination of things for the powerful soul, so that natural things are affected by it and are subjected. But in this sense, according to them, it is very limited, so it does not reach the point of transforming the very essences of things, but rather like moving the air, for example. (2) The scholar al-Hafiz al-Shami in 'Subul al-Huda wa al-Rashad' transmitted from al-Amidi who said: (After al-Amidi related the philosophers' doctrine on prophethood, and the saying of those who say that the prophet knows himself to be a prophet, and the saying of those who say that prophethood is an embassy between the Truth and creation, and he refuted each, he said: The truth is what the people of truth among the Ash'aris and others have held, that prophethood is not reducible to an essential attribute of the prophet's essence, nor to an acquired accident of his, but it is a gift from Allah and a favor from Him upon him that makes him reflect on messengership. Its net result is that Allah says to whom He chooses from His servants: 'I have sent you' or 'I have commissioned you, so convey from Me.' End quote.) Thus it is known that prophethood and messengership are relational attributes (al-sifaat al-i'tibariyya), like sainthood for the saint and imamate for the sultan, and so on; because speech does not necessitate an attribute for its object, as Qadi 'Adud al-Din stated.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary on the line 'And prophethood was not acquired.' It begins by defining the Muslim position: the servant does not acquire prophethood by any specific actions or practices, contrary to the philosophers. The author explains that Muslims interpret prophethood as a special divine gift whereby the servant receives revelation of a legal ruling, whether or not he is commanded to convey it; messengership adds the condition of conveyance. The philosophers, however, view prophethood as acquired through spiritual exercises that purify the soul. The disagreement is rooted in differing definitions. The author then states that the philosophers' claim of acquisition is one of the strongest grounds for declaring them disbelievers, even if not explicitly mentioned in the famous poem. He then argues that their view necessarily allows for the possibility of a prophet after Muhammad, which contradicts the Quran (Ahzab:40) and the hadith 'There is no prophet after me,' and the consensus of the community. The passage includes two footnotes: the first explains the philosophers' view that miracles are acquired, limited to certain effects; the second transmits al-Amidi's position that prophethood is not an essential attribute or acquired accident but a divine gift, making it a relational attribute (sifa i'tibariyya) similar to sainthood or imamate, since the divine address does not create a real attribute in the person. The conclusion clarifies that prophethood and messengership are such attributes.

Key Terms
الصفات الاعتبارية
الرسالة
المعجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think prophethood is an inherent quality like intelligence.
Correction: The passage explains it is a relational attribute conferred by Allah's address, not an inherent trait.

Checkpoint
According to al-Amidi, what is prophethood?
A) A natural talent
B) An acquired skill
C) A divine gift and relational attribute
D) A state of purity

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' claim leads to denying the finality of prophethood, and the correct view is that prophethood is a relational attribute granted by divine choice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you secretly believe that you can earn Allah's favor through your own efforts, just as the philosophers thought prophethood could be acquired? How does this passage challenge that assumption in your own life?
?
If prophethood were acquired, could another prophet come after Muhammad? Are you absolutely certain that Muhammad is the final prophet, or do you entertain doubts? What would it mean for your faith if you were wrong?
?
When you see a miracle described in the Quran or Sunnah, do you view it as a direct act of Allah or do you rationalize it as a natural phenomenon? How does your answer reflect your understanding of prophethood as a divine gift?

The Two Types of Sainthood (Wilayah)
Commentary classifies sainthood into acquired and non-acquired types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between acquired and non-acquired sainthood according to the commentary.

Core Idea
Sainthood has two paths: one earned by obedience, one granted by divine favor.

The commentator begins by addressing the concept of sainthood (wilayah), explaining that it is not a single, undifferentiated state. Rather, there are two distinct types: one that is acquired through human effort, and another that is purely a divine gift. This classification helps us understand the different ways closeness to Allah is attained.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage identifying the two types
Read the Arabic passage once, noting the two categories mentioned: acquired (muktasab) and non-acquired (ghayr muktasab). Try to find the defining characteristics of each.
The passage uses the term 'al-wilaya al-'amma' for the acquired type.
2
Understand the definitions
Acquired sainthood is defined as compliance with commands and avoidance of prohibitions. Non-acquired sainthood includes divine gifts like inspired knowledge (al-'ilm al-ladunni) and vision of the Preserved Tablet.
Note that the non-acquired type is not earned by effort.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why is it important to distinguish these two types? This shows that some aspects of closeness to Allah are gifts, not achievements.
This connects to the broader lesson that prophethood is also a gift.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الولاية ففيها طريقتان، والأظهر التفصيل، فمنها ما هو مكتسب؛ وهو امتثال المأمورات واجتناب المنهيات وتُسمَّى الولاية العامة ومنها ما هو غير مكتسب؛ وهو العطايا الربانية كالعلم اللدني ورؤية اللوح المحفوظ وغير ذلك. قوله : (بَلْ ذَاكَ فَضْلُ اللهِ يُؤْتِيهِ لِمَنْ يَشَاءُ جَلَّ اللهُ وَاهِبُ المِنَنْ قوله : (بَلْ ذَاكَ فَضْلُ اللهِ هذا إضراب انتقاليّ لا إبطالي، واسم الإشارة عائد على المذكور من النبوة. والفضل : إعطاء الشيء بغير عوض لا عاجل ولا ،آجل، ولذا لا يكون لغيره تعالى، وفي الكلام حذف مضاف والتقدير : بل المذكور من النبوة أثر فضل الله، وقد فسَّرَ الشارح اسم الإشارة بالاصطفاء للنبوة والاختيار للرسالة، وعليه فلا حاجة لتقدير المضاف المذكور، وإن قدره الشارحُ مع ذلك التفسير؛ لأن الاصطفاء للنبوة والاختيار للرسالة جُزئي من جزئيات فضل الله لا أثره. وقوله : (يُؤْتِيهِ لِمَنْ يَشَاءُ ) أي : آتاه وأعطاه لمن شاءه وأراده في الأزل لذلك ممن كان مستجمعاً لشروط النبوة، فالمراد بالمضارع الماضي فيهما، وإنما عبر بالمضارع استحضاراً للصورة العجيبة وإنما كان المضارع بمعنى الماضي في الأول؛ لأن إيتاء النبوة قد انقطع بعده ، فإنه خاتم النبيين، وفي الثاني لأن مشيئته وإرادته تعالى لذلك ثابتة فى الأزل، وإن تأخَّرَ الإيتاء بالفعل فيما لا يزال والضمير المنصوب في
As for sainthood (al-wilaya), there are two paths, and the most apparent is the detailed view: some of it is acquired – that is, compliance with commands and avoidance of prohibitions, and it is called general sainthood; and some of it is non-acquired – that is, divine gifts such as knowledge by direct inspiration (al-'ilm al-ladunni), vision of the Preserved Tablet, and so forth. His saying: (Rather, that is the favor of Allah; He gives it to whom He wills; exalted is Allah, the Bestower of gifts.) His saying: (Rather, that is the favor of Allah) – this is a transitional shift (idrab intiqali), not an invalidating one. The demonstrative pronoun refers to what was mentioned about prophethood. Al-fadl (favor) is giving something without compensation, neither immediate nor deferred, and therefore it cannot be from other than Him. In the sentence, there is a deleted construct, and the estimation is: 'Rather, what was mentioned of prophethood is the effect of Allah's favor.' The commentator interpreted the demonstrative pronoun as the selection for prophethood and the choice for messengership; accordingly, there is no need to estimate the mentioned construct, even if the commentator estimated it along with that interpretation, because the selection for prophethood and the choice for messengership are particulars of Allah's favor, not its effect. His saying: (He gives it to whom He wills) – that is, He gave and granted it to whom He willed and intended in pre-eternity for that, from among those who possessed the conditions of prophethood. So the present tense is intended as past in both places. It is expressed with the present tense to evoke a wondrous image. The present tense means past in the first because the giving of prophethood has ceased after him, for he is the seal of the prophets; and in the second because His will and intention for that are established in pre-eternity, even if the actual giving is delayed in the future. And the object pronoun in...
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage is a two-part commentary. First, it classifies sainthood (al-wilaya) into two types: acquired and non-acquired. The acquired type is general sainthood, achieved by obeying commands and avoiding prohibitions. The non-acquired type consists of divine gifts like inspired knowledge (al-'ilm al-ladunni) and seeing the Preserved Tablet. Second, it explains the line 'Rather, that is the favor of Allah...' in relation to prophethood. The author clarifies that this is a transitional shift (idrab intiqali), not a contradiction. The term 'favor' (al-fadl) means giving without compensation, exclusive to Allah. The phrase involves an implied construct: prophethood is an effect of divine favor. Alternatively, the demonstrative refers to the very selection for prophethood, which is itself a particular instance of favor, not merely an effect. The verb in the present tense is used for a past action: Allah gave prophethood to whom He willed in pre-eternity, but since Muhammad is the last prophet, the giving has ceased. The present tense evokes the wondrous nature of the act. The passage ends mid-sentence, continuing the grammatical analysis of the pronoun.

Key Terms
الولاية
مكتسب
العطايا الربانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All sainthood is achieved by one's own effort.
Correction: Some sainthood is a pure gift from Allah, not attained by effort.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the acquired type of sainthood (al-wilaya)?
A) Vision of the Preserved Tablet.
B) Knowledge by direct inspiration (al-'ilm al-ladunni).
C) Compliance with commands and avoidance of prohibitions.
D) The selection for prophethood.

Key Takeaway
Sainthood includes both an earned dimension through obedience and an unearned dimension through divine favor.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which path to closeness with Allah have you been neglecting: the path of obedience (acquired) or the path of receiving divine gifts (non-acquired)? What is one concrete change you can make this week to pursue the one you neglect?
?
When you experience a moment of spiritual insight or a sudden increase in understanding of your deen, do you attribute it to your own efforts or recognize it as a divine gift from Allah? How would this recognition change your gratitude and humility?
?
If sainthood is partly earned and partly granted, are you relying too much on your deeds or too little on Allah's mercy? How can you strike a balance between working hard in 'ibadah and humbly asking for His pure favor?

Prophethood as Pure Divine Favor
Commentary explains that prophethood is a divine favor and analyzes the Quranic verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophethood is a pure gift from Allah, not earned or deserved.

Core Idea
Prophethood is Allah's unmerited favor, given without compensation.

The commentary now turns to a key theological point: prophethood is not something that can be acquired; it is purely a favor (fadl) from Allah. This is explained through grammatical analysis of the Quranic phrase 'Rather, that is the favor of Allah...' The commentator clarifies that the demonstrative refers to the selection for prophethood, which is itself a specific instance of divine favor.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on divine favor
Read the Arabic passage focusing on the definition of 'favor' (al-fadl). Notice how the commentator explains the phrase 'Rather, that is the favor of Allah.'
The commentator describes this as a transitional shift (idrab intiqali), not a correction.
2
Understand the grammatical analysis
The commentator notes a deleted construct in the sentence and offers two interpretations: either the prophethood is an effect of favor, or the very selection for prophethood is a part of favor.
The second interpretation avoids the need to estimate a deleted word.
3
Grasp the theological implication
Prophethood is given by Allah's will alone, without compensation, and it ceased after the Prophet Muhammad. Reflect on what this means about human effort in attaining prophethood.
The present tense verb is used to evoke wonder, but refers to past action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Prophet ﷺ received the greatest favor, yet he was the most grateful. When you recite the Quran or learn about the Sunnah, do you receive it as a gift or an obligation? Tomorrow, before reading the Quran, say: 'This is a favor from Allah.'
?
Allah gives His favor to whom He wills, not based on your worth. Have you ever looked down on someone less religious, thinking you deserved Allah's guidance more? Repent from that pride and ask Allah to grant guidance to all.

The Absolute Superiority of the Prophet Muhammad
Commentator asserts absolute superiority of Prophet Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Prophet Muhammad is considered the best of all creation, according to classical Sunni theology.

Core Idea
Prophet Muhammad is superior to all creatures without exception.

One of the most distinctive beliefs in Sunni Islam is that Prophet Muhammad ﷺ is the greatest being ever created. This short but powerful statement from the poem declares his absolute superiority over all creatures, including angels and other prophets. Let's examine how the commentator unpacks this doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic phrase
Read the Arabic line from the poem: 'وَأَفْضَلُ الخَلْقِ عَلَى الإِطْلَاقِ نَبِيُّنا'. Notice the key words 'أفضل' (best), 'الخلق' (creation), and 'على الإطلاق' (absolutely).
This phrase is a complete assertion of rank.
2
Understand the commentator's explanation
The commentator rephrases the line as 'أفضل المخلوقات على العموم' (the best of created beings in general). The phrase 'على الإطلاق' is interpreted as 'absolutely' or 'generally' meaning without any restriction or exception.
The commentator is clarifying that 'على الإطلاق' does not limit the superiority to a certain type of creature.
3
Reflect on the theological significance
Consider why this doctrine matters: it affirms that the Prophet ﷺ ranks above all other beings, including angels and previous prophets. This belief is a cornerstone of Sunni reverence for the Prophet.
This does not diminish the status of angels or other prophets; it simply establishes their relative rank.
4
Address a common misunderstanding
Some might think that angels or other prophets could be equal or even superior to Muhammad. This passage explicitly rejects that notion by using 'على الإطلاق' (absolutely).
The doctrine is clear: the Prophet is the best of all creation without exception.

His saying: (And the best of creation absolutely is our Prophet:) means: the best of created beings in general.

The commentator interprets it as meaning the best of all created beings in a general sense (afḍalu l-makhlūqāti ʿalā l-ʿumūm). This affirms the doctrine that Prophet Muhammad is superior to all other creatures, including angels and other prophets, without any exception or qualification.

The Absolute Best of Creation: Prophet Muhammad
Declares Prophet Muhammad as best of creation and notes consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author declares Prophet Muhammad as the absolute best of creation and how this is a matter of consensus.

Core Idea
Prophet Muhammad is the best of all creation, a consensus even among the Mu'tazila.

The author begins by firmly establishing that our Prophet Muhammad is the absolute best of creation. He defines 'best' comprehensively, covering all creatures—humans, jinn, and angels—in all qualities of good. He also notes the grammatical structure of the line and emphasizes that this is a consensus among Muslims, including the Mu'tazila, thereby excluding the Prophet from the later debate on angels vs. humans.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Notice the strong declaration of superiority.
2
Identify the scope of 'best of creation'
The author explains that 'best of creation' includes all creatures (higher and lower, humans, jinn, angels) in this world and the Hereafter.
This is a comprehensive superiority.
3
Understand the grammatical construction
The author notes that 'best of creation' can be a preceding predicate and 'our Prophet' a delayed subject, or vice versa. The 'our' is for honor, not specification.
Grammar serves theology.
4
Recognize the consensus
The superiority of the Prophet is an agreed-upon matter among Muslims, even the Mu'tazila. This excludes him from the later disagreement between angels and humans.
Consensus strengthens the doctrine.
5
Reflect on the implications
Think about why the author emphasizes this point at the start. How does it set the stage for refuting objections?
Compare with the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَفْضَلُ الخَلْقِ عَلَى الإِطْلَاقِ نَبِيُّنا فَمِلْ عَنِ الشَّقَاقِ قوله : (وَأَفْضَلُ الخَلْقِ عَلَى الإِطْلاقِ نَبِيُّنا :أي: أفضل المخلوقات على العموم الشامل للعلوية والسفلية من البشر والجن والملك في الدنيا والآخرة في سائر خصال الخير وأوصاف الكمال.. نبينا محمد ، والأولى أن (أفضل الخلق) خبر مُقدَّم، و(نبينا) مبتدأ مُؤخَرٌ ، ويصح العكس، والإضافة في (نبينا) لتشريف المضاف إليه، لا للاختصاص؛ لما سيأتي من عموم بعثته ، هذا إذا جعل الضمير راجعاً لهذه الأمة، وإن جعل لما يشمل هذه الأمة وغيرها كان عاما مطابقاً؛ لما سيأتي من عموم بعثته . وأفضليته صلى الله عليه وسلم على جميع المخلوقات ممَّا أجمع عليه المسلمون حتى المعتزلة، فهو مُستثنى من الخلاف الآتي في التفضيل بين الملائكة والبشر، ولا عبرة بما زعمه الزمخشري من تفضيل جبريل عليه مستدلا بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّهُ لَقَولُ رَسُولِ كَرِيمٍ) کو التكوير : ۱۹] الآية حيث عدَّ فيه فضائل جبريل، فإنه وصف فيه بأنه رسول كريم إلى قوله : (أمين التكوير : (۲۱)، واقتصر على نفى الجنون عنه بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا صَاحِبكم بمجنون التكوير : ۲۲] وقد خرق في ذلك الإجماع، ولا دلالة في الآية لما ادعاه ؛ لأنَّ المقصود منها نفي قولهم : ﴿إِنَّما يُعلَمُهُ بَسر ﴾ [النحل : ١٠٣]، وقولهم أَفَتَرَى عَلَى اللَّهِ كَذِبًا بِهِ جِنَّةٌ [سبا : ۸] ، وليس المقصود المفاضلة بينهما، وإنما هو شيء اقتضاه الحال، ولا عبرة بما قد يتوهم من تفضيل جبريل عليه، لكونه كان يعلمه ، فكم من معلم - بالفتح - أفضل من معلم - بالكسر
And the best of creation absolutely is our Prophet, so turn away from dissension. His statement: (And the best of creation absolutely is our Prophet) meaning: the best of creatures in generality encompassing the higher and lower realms, of humans, jinn, and angels, in this world and the Hereafter, in all qualities of good and attributes of perfection: our Prophet Muhammad. And it is better that (the best of creation) is a preceding predicate, and (our Prophet) is a delayed subject; the opposite is also permissible. The addition in (our Prophet) is for the honor of the one added to, not for specification, because of what will come of the universality of his mission. This if the pronoun refers to this nation; if it refers to what includes this nation and others, it is universally consistent because of the universality of his mission. And his superiority, peace be upon him, over all creatures is something upon which the Muslims have agreed, even the Mu'tazila. So he is excluded from the coming disagreement about preference between angels and humans. And no consideration is given to what al-Zamakhshari claimed of preferring Jibril over him, arguing with His statement, exalted: "And indeed it is the word of a noble messenger" (Surat al-Takwir, 19) and onward, where he enumerated Jibril's virtues. For he described him as a noble messenger up to his statement: "trustworthy" (al-Takwir, 21), and restricted himself to negating madness from him with His statement: "And your companion is not mad" (al-Takwir, 22). He thus broke the consensus in that. There is no indication in the verse for what he claimed, because the purpose of it was to refute their saying: "Only a human teaches him" (al-Nahl, 103) and their saying: "Has he invented a lie about Allah or is there madness in him?" (Saba', 8). The purpose was not preference between them; rather it was something required by the situation. And no regard is given to what might be imagined of preferring Jibril over him because he used to teach him, for how many a teacher (with fatha on the first letter) is better than a teacher (with kasra).
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage explains the line from the poem declaring that our Prophet Muhammad is the absolute best of creation. The commentary begins by defining 'best of creation' as encompassing all creatures—humans, jinn, angels, in this world and the Hereafter. Grammatically, it notes that 'best of creation' can be a preceding predicate and 'our Prophet' a delayed subject, or vice versa. The addition 'our' in 'our Prophet' is for honor, not specification, given the universality of his mission. The author then asserts that the Prophet's superiority over all creation is a matter of consensus among Muslims, including the Mu'tazila, thus excluding him from the debate on whether angels or humans are superior. The passage refutes al-Zamakhshari's claim that Jibril is superior based on Quranic verses from Surat al-Takwir. The refutation argues that these verses were intended to refute accusations that the Prophet was taught by a human or was mad, not to compare Jibril and Muhammad. It further points out that even if Jibril taught the Prophet, a teacher (mu'allim, with fatha) can be less than the student (mu'allam, with kasra), implying that being a teacher does not necessitate superiority.

Key Terms
أفضل الخلق
نبينا
إجماع
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author say about the consensus on the Prophet's superiority?
A) It is agreed upon by all Muslims except the Mu'tazila.
B) It is agreed upon by all Muslims including the Mu'tazila.
C) It is a disputed matter among scholars.
D) It applies only to humans, not angels.

Key Takeaway
Prophet Muhammad is the absolute best of creation, a point of consensus among all Muslims.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet is the absolute best of creation, what does your daily schedule reveal about your actual belief in his superiority?
?
The author commands to 'turn away from dissension.' Where in your heart do you harbor doubt or argument about the Prophet's status?
?
The Mu'tazila agreed on this despite other differences. Are you quick to agree with fellow Muslims on what unites us, or do you focus on differences?

Refuting the Claim of Jibril's Superiority
Refutes Zamakhshari's argument for Jibril's superiority using context and analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Zamakhshari's argument from Surat al-Takwir fails to prove Jibril's superiority over the Prophet.

Core Idea
The verses cited by Zamakhshari refute accusations, not establish Jibril's superiority.

The author addresses a specific objection from al-Zamakhshari, who argued that Jibril is superior to the Prophet based on Quranic verses describing Jibril as a noble messenger and trustworthy. The author refutes this by showing the context of those verses: they were revealed to reject the polytheists' claims that the Prophet was taught by a human or was mad. The author also provides an analogy that a teacher (mu'allim) is not necessarily superior to the student (mu'allam).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English carefully. Note the refutation of Zamakhshari's evidence.
Focus on the logical argument.
2
Identify Zamakhshari's claim
Zamakhshari argued that Jibril is superior because the Quran calls him 'noble messenger' and 'trustworthy' and denies madness of the Prophet.
His proof is from Surat al-Takwir.
3
Understand the author's refutation
The author says these verses were meant to refute accusations that the Prophet was taught by a human or was mad—they are not about comparing the two.
Context is key.
4
Examine the teacher-student analogy
The author points out that a teacher (mu'allim) can be less than the student (mu'allam). Teaching does not imply superiority.
This weakens the assumption that Jibril is superior because he taught the Prophet.
5
Reflect on the outcome
Zamakhshari's claim breaks consensus and lacks evidence. The Prophet's superiority remains unshaken.
Think about how this refutation preserves the doctrine.
